      <p><b>Eritrea</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/Ë/: secondary stress follows">Ë</span><span title="/Ér/: 'err' in 'merry'">Ér</span><span title="/Éª/: 'i' in 'kit'">Éª</span><span title="/Ë/: primary stress follows">Ë</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="'r' in 'rye'">r</span><span title="/eÉª/: 'a' in 'face'">eÉª</span><span title="/É/: 'a' in 'about'">É</span></span>,<span class="wrap"> </span><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/Ë/: secondary stress follows">Ë</span><span title="/Ér/: 'err' in 'merry'">Ér</span><span title="/Éª/: 'i' in 'kit'">Éª</span><span title="/Ë/: primary stress follows">Ë</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="'r' in 'rye'">r</span><span title="/iË/: 'ee' in 'fleece'">iË</span><span title="/É/: 'a' in 'about'">É</span></span>/</a></span></span><sup id="cite_ref-:0_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-19">[19]</a></sup> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ertra.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/3d/Ertra.ogg" class="internal" title="Ertra.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span>),<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> officially the <b>State of Eritrea</b>, is a country in <a href="/wiki/East_Africa" title="East Africa">Eastern Africa</a>, with its capital at <a href="/wiki/Asmara" title="Asmara">Asmara</a>. It is bordered by <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a> in the south, <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a> in the west, and <a href="/wiki/Djibouti" title="Djibouti">Djibouti</a> in the southeast. The northeastern and eastern parts of Eritrea have an extensive coastline along the <a href="/wiki/Red_Sea" title="Red Sea">Red Sea</a>. The nation has a total area of approximately 117,600&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (45,406&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi), and includes the <a href="/wiki/Dahlak_Archipelago" title="Dahlak Archipelago">Dahlak Archipelago</a> and several of the <a href="/wiki/Hanish_Islands" title="Hanish Islands">Hanish Islands</a>. </p>
      <p>Eritrea is a multi-ethnic country, with nine recognized ethnic groups in its population of around six and a half million. Eritrea has nine national languages which are <a href="/wiki/Tigrinya_language" title="Tigrinya language">Tigrinya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tigre_language" title="Tigre language">Tigre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Afar_language" title="Afar language">Afar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beja_language" title="Beja language">Beja</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bilen_language" title="Bilen language">Bilen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kunama_language" title="Kunama language">Kunama</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nara_language" title="Nara language">Nara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saho_language" title="Saho language">Saho</a>. <a href="/wiki/Tigrinya_language" title="Tigrinya language">Tigrinya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arabic" title="Arabic">Arabic</a>, and <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> serve as the three working languages.<sup id="cite_ref-MOI_Eritrea_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MOI_Eritrea-2">[2]</a></sup> Most residents speak languages from the <a href="/wiki/Afroasiatic_languages" title="Afroasiatic languages">Afroasiatic</a> family, either of the <a href="/wiki/Ethiopian_Semitic_languages" title="Ethiopian Semitic languages">Ethiopian Semitic languages</a> or <a href="/wiki/Cushitic_languages" title="Cushitic languages">Cushitic</a> branches. Among these communities, the <a href="/wiki/Tigrigni" class="mw-redirect" title="Tigrigni">Tigrinyas</a> make up about 55% of the population, with the <a href="/wiki/Tigre_people" title="Tigre people">Tigre people</a> constituting around 30% of inhabitants. In addition, there are a number of <a href="/wiki/Nilo-Saharan_languages" title="Nilo-Saharan languages">Nilo-Saharan</a>-speaking <a href="/wiki/Nilotic" class="mw-redirect" title="Nilotic">Nilotic</a> ethnic groups. Most people in the territory adhere to <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> or <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>, with a small minority adhering to <a href="/wiki/Traditional_African_religions" title="Traditional African religions">traditional faiths</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-21">[21]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Aksum" title="Kingdom of Aksum">Kingdom of Aksum</a>, covering much of modern-day Eritrea and <a href="/wiki/Tigray_Region" title="Tigray Region">northern Ethiopia</a>, was established during the first or second century AD.<sup id="cite_ref-Munro-Hay57_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Munro-Hay57-22">[22]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Paul_B._Henze_2005_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Paul_B._Henze_2005-23">[23]</a></sup> It adopted <a href="/wiki/Eritrean_Orthodox_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Eritrean Orthodox Church">Christianity</a> around the middle of the fourth century.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> In medieval times much of Eritrea fell under the <a href="/wiki/Medri_Bahri" title="Medri Bahri">Medri Bahri</a> kingdom, with a smaller region being part of <a href="/wiki/Hamasien" title="Hamasien">Hamasien</a>. The creation of modern-day Eritrea is a result of the incorporation of independent, distinct kingdoms (for example, <a href="/wiki/Medri_Bahri" title="Medri Bahri">Medri Bahri</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Sultanate_of_Aussa" title="Sultanate of Aussa">Sultanate of Aussa</a>) eventually resulting in the formation of <a href="/wiki/Italian_Eritrea" title="Italian Eritrea">Italian Eritrea</a>. After the defeat of the Italian colonial army in 1942, Eritrea was administered by the <a href="/wiki/British_Military_Administration_(Eritrea)" class="mw-redirect" title="British Military Administration (Eritrea)">British Military Administration</a> until 1952. Following the UN General Assembly decision, in 1952, Eritrea would govern itself with a local Eritrean parliament, but for foreign affairs and defense it would enter into a federal status with Ethiopia for a period of 10 years. However, in 1962 the government of Ethiopia annulled the Eritrean parliament and formally annexed Eritrea. The Eritrean secessionist movement organized the <a href="/wiki/Eritrean_Liberation_Front" title="Eritrean Liberation Front">Eritrean Liberation Front</a> in 1961 and fought the <a href="/wiki/Eritrean_War_of_Independence" title="Eritrean War of Independence">Eritrean War of Independence</a> until Eritrea gained <i>de facto</i> independence in 1991. Eritrea gained <i>de jure</i> independence in 1993 after <a href="/wiki/1993_Eritrean_independence_referendum" title="1993 Eritrean independence referendum">an independence referendum</a>. </p>
      <p>Eritrea is a unitary <a href="/wiki/One-party" class="mw-redirect" title="One-party">one-party</a> presidential republic in which <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_Eritrea" title="Elections in Eritrea">national legislative and presidential elections</a> have never been held since independence.<sup id="cite_ref-gi_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gi-25">[25]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Eritreaâs_Silent_Totalitarianism_-_McGill_Journal_of_Political_Studies_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eritreaâs_Silent_Totalitarianism_-_McGill_Journal_of_Political_Studies-9">[9]</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Eritrea" title="Human rights in Eritrea">Eritrean government's human rights record</a> is among the worst in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-hrw_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hrw-26">[26]</a></sup> The Eritrean government has dismissed these allegations as politically motivated.<sup id="cite_ref-Tesf_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tesf-27">[27]</a></sup> Because all local media is state-owned, Eritrea was also ranked as having the third-least press freedom in the global <a href="/wiki/Press_Freedom_Index" title="Press Freedom Index">Press Freedom Index</a>, behind <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Turkmenistan" title="Turkmenistan">Turkmenistan</a>. </p>
      <p>Eritrea is a member of the <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmental_Authority_on_Development" title="Intergovernmental Authority on Development">Intergovernmental Authority on Development</a>, and is an <a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_the_Arab_League#List_of_current_observer_states" title="Member states of the Arab League">observer state</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Arab_League" title="Arab League">Arab League</a> alongside <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-edition.cnn.com_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-edition.cnn.com-28">[28]</a></sup> </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Name">Name</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Name">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>The name <i>Eritrea</i> is derived from the ancient Greek name for the <a href="/wiki/Red_Sea" title="Red Sea">Red Sea</a> (<span lang="grc" title="Ancient Greek (to 1453)-language text"><a href="/wiki/Erythraean_Sea" title="Erythraean Sea">á¼ÏÏÎ¸Ïá½° ÎÎ¬Î»Î±ÏÏÎ±</a></span> <i lang="grc-Latn" title="Ancient Greek (to 1453)-language text">Erythra Thalassa</i>, based on the adjective <span lang="grc" title="Ancient Greek (to 1453)-language text">á¼ÏÏÎ¸ÏÏÏ</span> <i lang="grc-Latn" title="Ancient Greek (to 1453)-language text">erythros</i> "red"). It was first formally adopted in 1890, with the formation of <a href="/wiki/Italian_Eritrea" title="Italian Eritrea">Italian Eritrea</a> (<i>Colonia Eritrea</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-ConnellKillion2010_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ConnellKillion2010-29">[29]</a></sup> The name persisted over the course of subsequent <a href="/wiki/British_Military_Administration_(Eritrea)" class="mw-redirect" title="British Military Administration (Eritrea)">British</a> and <a href="/wiki/Federation_of_Ethiopia_and_Eritrea" title="Federation of Ethiopia and Eritrea">Ethiopian</a> occupation, and was reaffirmed by the <a href="/wiki/Eritrean_independence_referendum,_1993" class="mw-redirect" title="Eritrean independence referendum, 1993">1993 independence referendum</a> and <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Eritrea" title="Constitution of Eritrea">1997 constitution</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Eritrea" title="History of Eritrea">History of Eritrea</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistory">Prehistory</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Prehistory">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <table role="presentation" class="metadata mbox-small noprint selfref" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000;width: 22em;"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <td class="mbox-image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Ge%27ez.svg/40px-Ge%27ez.svg.png" decoding="async" width="40" height="22" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Ge%27ez.svg/60px-Ge%27ez.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Ge%27ez.svg/80px-Ge%27ez.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="219" data-file-height="120"></td> 
         <td class="mbox-text plainlist" style="vertical-align:middle; font-size:95%;">You may need <a href="/wiki/Help:Multilingual_support_(Ethiopic)" title="Help:Multilingual support (Ethiopic)">rendering support</a> to display the <a href="/wiki/Ge%27ez_script" class="mw-redirect" title="Ge'ez script">Ethiopic text</a> in this article correctly.</td>
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>Buya in Eritrea, one of the oldest <a href="/wiki/Hominid" class="mw-redirect" title="Hominid">hominids</a> representing a possible link between <i><a href="/wiki/Homo_erectus" title="Homo erectus">Homo erectus</a></i> and an archaic <i><a href="/wiki/Human" title="Human">Homo sapiens</a></i> was found by Italian scientists. Dated to over 1&nbsp;million years old, it is the oldest skeletal find of its kind and provides a link between hominids and the earliest <a href="/wiki/Anatomically_modern_humans" class="mw-redirect" title="Anatomically modern humans">anatomically modern humans</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> It is believed that the section of the <a href="/wiki/Danakil_Depression" title="Danakil Depression">Danakil Depression</a> in Eritrea was also a major player in terms of human evolution, and may contain other traces of evolution from <i>Homo erectus</i> hominids to anatomically modern humans.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>During the last interglacial period, the <a href="/wiki/Red_Sea" title="Red Sea">Red Sea</a> coast of Eritrea was occupied by early anatomically modern humans.<sup id="cite_ref-pmid10811218_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pmid10811218-33">[33]</a></sup> It is believed that the area was on the route out of Africa that some scholars suggest was used by early humans to colonize the rest of the Old World.<sup id="cite_ref-pmid10811218_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pmid10811218-33">[33]</a></sup> In 1999, the Eritrean Research Project Team composed of Eritrean, Canadian, American, Dutch and French scientists discovered a <a href="/wiki/Paleolithic" title="Paleolithic">Paleolithic</a> site with stone and obsidian tools dated to over 125,000 years old near the Bay of Zula south of <a href="/wiki/Massawa" title="Massawa">Massawa</a>, along the Red Sea littoral. The tools are believed to have been used by early humans to harvest marine resources such as clams and oysters.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> <sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Blench143144_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Blench143144-37">[37]</a></sup> </p> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle .thumbcaption{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow>.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style>
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Kohaito,_grotta_di_adi_alauti_con_pitture_rupestri_databili_al_2500_ac_ca._14_bestiame.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Kohaito%2C_grotta_di_adi_alauti_con_pitture_rupestri_databili_al_2500_ac_ca._14_bestiame.JPG/200px-Kohaito%2C_grotta_di_adi_alauti_con_pitture_rupestri_databili_al_2500_ac_ca._14_bestiame.JPG" decoding="async" width="200" height="133" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Kohaito%2C_grotta_di_adi_alauti_con_pitture_rupestri_databili_al_2500_ac_ca._14_bestiame.JPG/300px-Kohaito%2C_grotta_di_adi_alauti_con_pitture_rupestri_databili_al_2500_ac_ca._14_bestiame.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Kohaito%2C_grotta_di_adi_alauti_con_pitture_rupestri_databili_al_2500_ac_ca._14_bestiame.JPG/400px-Kohaito%2C_grotta_di_adi_alauti_con_pitture_rupestri_databili_al_2500_ac_ca._14_bestiame.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="2304"></a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Qohaito,_Eritrea_(33628113490).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Qohaito%2C_Eritrea_%2833628113490%29.jpg/200px-Qohaito%2C_Eritrea_%2833628113490%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Qohaito%2C_Eritrea_%2833628113490%29.jpg/300px-Qohaito%2C_Eritrea_%2833628113490%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Qohaito%2C_Eritrea_%2833628113490%29.jpg/400px-Qohaito%2C_Eritrea_%2833628113490%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="3456"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           Neolithic rock art in a <a href="/wiki/Qohaito" title="Qohaito">Qohaito</a> canyon cave, Pre-Axumite monolithic columns in <a href="/wiki/Qohaito" title="Qohaito">Qohaito</a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Antiquity">Antiquity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Antiquity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Gash_Group" title="Gash Group">Gash Group</a>, <a href="/wiki/Land_of_punt" class="mw-redirect" title="Land of punt">Land of punt</a>, and <a href="/wiki/D%CA%BFmt" title="DÊ¿mt">DÊ¿mt</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Research shows tools found in the Barka Valley dating from 8000 BC appear to offer the first concrete evidence of human settlement in the area.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> Research also shows that many of the ethnic groups of Eritrea were the first to inhabit these areas.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Excavations in and near <a href="/wiki/Agordat" title="Agordat">Agordat</a> in central Eritrea yielded the remains of an ancient pre-Aksumite civilization known as the <a href="/wiki/Gash_Group" title="Gash Group">Gash Group</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Leclant402_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Leclant402-40">[40]</a></sup> Ceramics were discovered that were dating back between 2500â1500 BC.<sup id="cite_ref-Cole_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cole-41">[41]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Around 2000 BC, parts of Eritrea were most likely part of the <a href="/wiki/Land_of_Punt" title="Land of Punt">Land of Punt</a>, first mentioned in the 25th century BC.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-independent.co.uk_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-independent.co.uk-43">[43]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> It was known for producing and exporting <a href="/wiki/Gold" title="Gold">gold</a>, aromatic <a href="/wiki/Resin" title="Resin">resins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dalbergia_melanoxylon" title="Dalbergia melanoxylon">blackwood</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ebony" title="Ebony">ebony</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ivory_trade" title="Ivory trade">ivory</a> and wild animals. The region is known from ancient Egyptian records of trade expeditions to it.<sup id="cite_ref-Shaw_&amp;_Nicholson,_p.231_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shaw_&amp;_Nicholson,_p.231-45">[45]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:210_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:210-46">[46]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:1_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-47">[47]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:2_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-48">[48]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Excavations at <a href="/wiki/Sembel" title="Sembel">Sembel</a> found evidence of an ancient pre-<a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Aksum" title="Kingdom of Aksum">Aksumite</a> civilization in greater Asmara. This Ona urban culture is believed to have been among the earliest pastoral and agricultural communities in the region. Artifacts at the site have been dated to between 800 BC and 400 BC, contemporaneous with other pre-Aksumite settlements in the Eritrean and Ethiopian highlands during the mid-first millennium BC.<sup id="cite_ref-Schmidt_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schmidt-49">[49]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Avanzini_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Avanzini-50">[50]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span id="Kingdom_of_D.27mt"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Kingdom_of_D'mt">Kingdom of D'mt</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Kingdom of D'mt">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/D%CA%BFmt" title="DÊ¿mt">DÊ¿mt</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Leaping_Ibex,_Ethiopia_(2130266960).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Leaping_Ibex%2C_Ethiopia_%282130266960%29.jpg/220px-Leaping_Ibex%2C_Ethiopia_%282130266960%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Leaping_Ibex%2C_Ethiopia_%282130266960%29.jpg/330px-Leaping_Ibex%2C_Ethiopia_%282130266960%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Leaping_Ibex%2C_Ethiopia_%282130266960%29.jpg/440px-Leaping_Ibex%2C_Ethiopia_%282130266960%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3024" data-file-height="1998"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Leaping_Ibex,_Ethiopia_(2130266960).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Bronze oil lamp excavated at <a href="/wiki/Matara,_Eritrea" title="Matara, Eritrea">Matara</a>, dating from the <a href="/wiki/D%CA%BFmt" title="DÊ¿mt">Kingdom of DÊ¿mt</a> (1st century BCE or earlier)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/D%CA%BFmt" title="DÊ¿mt">DÊ¿mt</a> was a kingdom that encompassed most of Eritrea and the northern frontier of Ethiopia. The polity existed during the 10th to 5th centuries BC. Given the presence of a massive temple complex at <a href="/wiki/Yeha" title="Yeha">Yeha</a>, this area was most likely the kingdom's capital. <a href="/wiki/Qohaito" title="Qohaito">Qohaito</a>, often identified as the town of Koloe in the <i><a href="/wiki/Periplus_of_the_Erythraean_Sea" title="Periplus of the Erythraean Sea">Periplus of the Erythraean Sea</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> as well as <a href="/wiki/Matara,_Eritrea" title="Matara, Eritrea">Matara</a> were important ancient DÊ¿mt kingdom cities in southern Eritrea. </p>
      <p>The realm developed <a href="/wiki/Irrigation" title="Irrigation">irrigation</a> schemes, used <a href="/wiki/Plow" class="mw-redirect" title="Plow">plows</a>, grew <a href="/wiki/Millet" title="Millet">millet</a>, and made <a href="/wiki/Iron" title="Iron">iron</a> tools and weapons. After the fall of DÊ¿mt in the 5th century BC, the plateau came to be dominated by smaller successor kingdoms. This lasted until the rise of one of these polities during the first century, the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Aksum" title="Kingdom of Aksum">Kingdom of Aksum</a>, which was able to reunite the area.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Kingdom_of_Aksum">Kingdom of Aksum</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Kingdom of Aksum">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Aksum" title="Kingdom of Aksum">Kingdom of Aksum</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The Kingdom of Aksum was a trading empire centered in Eritrea and northern Ethiopia.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> It existed from approximately 100â940 AD, growing from the proto-Aksumite <a href="/wiki/Iron_Age" title="Iron Age">Iron Age</a> period around the 4th century BC to achieve prominence by the 1st century AD. </p>
      <p>According to the medieval <i>Liber Axumae</i> (<a href="/wiki/Book_of_Aksum" title="Book of Aksum">Book of Aksum</a>), Aksum's first capital, Mazaber, was built by Itiyopis, son of Cush.<sup id="cite_ref-Agrvt_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Agrvt-55">[55]</a></sup> The capital was later moved to <a href="/wiki/Axum" title="Axum">Aksum</a> in northern Ethiopia. The Kingdom used the name "Ethiopia" as early as the 4th century.<sup id="cite_ref-Munro-Hay57_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Munro-Hay57-22">[22]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Paul_B._Henze_2005_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Paul_B._Henze_2005-23">[23]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Aksumites erected a number of large <a href="/wiki/Stele" title="Stele">stelae</a>, which served a religious purpose in pre-<a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christian</a> times. One of these granite columns, the <a href="/wiki/Obelisk_of_Aksum" class="mw-redirect" title="Obelisk of Aksum">Obelisk of Aksum</a>, is the largest such structure in the world, standing at 90 feet (27 metres).<sup id="cite_ref-Eospvo_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eospvo-56">[56]</a></sup> Under <a href="/wiki/Ezana_of_Axum" title="Ezana of Axum">Ezana</a> (<a href="/wiki/Floruit" title="Floruit">fl.</a> 320â360), Aksum later adopted <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Munro-Hay_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Munro-Hay-57">[57]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> was the first <a href="/wiki/World_religion" class="mw-redirect" title="World religion">world religion</a> to be adopted in Eritrea and the oldest monastery in the country <a href="/wiki/Debre_Sina_(monastery)" title="Debre Sina (monastery)">Debre Sina (monastery)</a> was built during the 4th century. It is one of the oldest monasteries in <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a> and the world.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Debre_Libanos_(Eritrea)" title="Debre Libanos (Eritrea)">Debre Libanos</a>, the second oldest monastery was said to have been founded in the late fifth or early sixth century. Originally located in the village of Ham, it was moved to an inaccessible location on the edge of a cliff below the Ham plateau. Its church contains the Golden Gospel, a metal-covered bible dating to the 13th century during which Debre Libanos was an important seat of religious power.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the 7th century, early <a href="/wiki/Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim">Muslims</a> from <a href="/wiki/Mecca" title="Mecca">Mecca</a>, at least <a href="/wiki/Sahaba" class="mw-redirect" title="Sahaba">companions</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Prophets_and_messengers_in_Islam" title="Prophets and messengers in Islam">Islamic <i>NabÄ«</i></a>, (<a href="/wiki/Prophet" title="Prophet">Prophet</a>) <a href="/wiki/Muhammad" title="Muhammad">Muhammad</a>, sought refuge from <a href="/wiki/Quraysh" title="Quraysh">Qurayshi</a> <a href="/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims_by_the_Meccans" class="mw-redirect" title="Persecution of Muslims by the Meccans">persecution</a> by travelling to the kingdom, a journey known in <a href="/wiki/Islamic_history" class="mw-redirect" title="Islamic history">Islamic history</a> as the <a href="/wiki/Migration_to_Abyssinia" title="Migration to Abyssinia">First Hijrah</a>. They reportedly built the <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_oldest_mosques#Africa" title="List of the oldest mosques">first</a> African <a href="/wiki/Mosque" title="Mosque">mosque</a>, that is the <a href="/wiki/Mosque_of_the_Companions,_Massawa" title="Mosque of the Companions, Massawa">Mosque of the Companions, Massawa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Reid2012Massawa_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reid2012Massawa-60">[60]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The kingdom is mentioned in the <i>Periplus of the Erythraean Sea</i> as an important market place for <a href="/wiki/Ivory_trade" title="Ivory trade">ivory</a>, which was exported throughout the ancient world. Aksum was at the time ruled by <a href="/wiki/Zoskales" title="Zoskales">Zoskales</a>, who also governed the port of <a href="/wiki/Adulis" title="Adulis">Adulis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Periplusme_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Periplusme-61">[61]</a></sup> The Aksumite rulers facilitated trade by minting their own <a href="/wiki/Aksumite_currency" title="Aksumite currency">Aksumite currency</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Raffaele2007_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Raffaele2007-62">[62]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_Ages">Middle Ages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Middle Ages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Medri_Bahri">Medri Bahri</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Medri Bahri">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Medri_Bahri" title="Medri Bahri">Medri Bahri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Habesh_Eyalet" title="Habesh Eyalet">Habesh Eyalet</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sultanate_of_Aussa" title="Sultanate of Aussa">Sultanate of Aussa</a>
      </div> 
      <p>After the decline of Aksum, the Eritrean highlands were under the domain of <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christian</a> Kingdom of Medri Bahri, ruled by <a href="/wiki/Bahr_Negash" class="mw-redirect" title="Bahr Negash">Bahri Negus</a>. The area was then known as <i>Ma'ikele Bahri</i> ("between the seas/rivers", i.e. the land between the <a href="/wiki/Red_Sea" title="Red Sea">Red Sea</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Mareb_River" title="Mareb River">Mereb river</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> The entire coastal domain of Ma'ikele Bahri was under the <a href="/wiki/Adal_Sultanate" title="Adal Sultanate">Adal Sultanate</a> during the reign of Sultan <a href="/wiki/Badlay_ibn_Sa%27ad_ad-Din" title="Badlay ibn Sa'ad ad-Din">Badlay</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> The state was later reconquered by Ethiopian Emperors namely <a href="/wiki/Zara_Yaqob" title="Zara Yaqob">Zara Yaqob</a>, and renamed the <a href="/wiki/Medri_Bahri" title="Medri Bahri">Medri Bahri</a> ("Sea land" in Tigrinya, although it included some areas like <a href="/wiki/Shire,_Ethiopia" class="mw-redirect" title="Shire, Ethiopia">Shire in Ethiopia</a> on the other side of the Mereb, today in Ethiopia).<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> With its capital at <a href="/wiki/Debarwa" title="Debarwa">Debarwa</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> the state's main provinces were <a href="/wiki/Hamasien" title="Hamasien">Hamasien</a>, <a href="/wiki/Serae" title="Serae">Serae</a> and <a href="/wiki/Akele_Guzai" title="Akele Guzai">Akele Guzai</a>. </p>
      <p>The first Westerner to visit Eritrea was the Portuguese explorer <a href="/wiki/Francisco_%C3%81lvares" title="Francisco Ãlvares">Francisco Alvares</a> in 1520. In his books we have the first description of the local powers of Tigray, the kingdom of Axum and Barnagais (the lord of the lands by the sea)<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The coast of present-day Eritrea, was the one that guaranteed the connection to the region of Tigray where the Portuguese had a small colony, and therefore the connection to the interior <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopian</a>, allies of the Portuguese. Masswa was also the stage for the landing of troops by CristovÃ£o da Gama in the military campaign that would eventually defeat Adal in the final battle of <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Wayna_Daga" title="Battle of Wayna Daga">Wayna Daga</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bahta_Hagos.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f0/Bahta_Hagos.jpeg/170px-Bahta_Hagos.jpeg" decoding="async" width="170" height="238" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f0/Bahta_Hagos.jpeg/255px-Bahta_Hagos.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f0/Bahta_Hagos.jpeg/340px-Bahta_Hagos.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="456" data-file-height="638"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bahta_Hagos.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Bahta_Hagos" title="Bahta Hagos">Bahta Hagos</a> was an important leader of the Eritrean resistance to foreign domination specifically against northern Ethiopian and Italian colonialism.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In 1734, the <a href="/wiki/Afar_people" title="Afar people">Afar</a> leader Kedafu, established the <a href="/wiki/Mudaito_Dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Mudaito Dynasty">Mudaito Dynasty</a> in Ethiopia, which later also came to include the southern Denkel lowlands of Eritrea, thus incorporating the southern denkel lowlands to the <a href="/wiki/Sultanate_of_Aussa" title="Sultanate of Aussa">Sultanate of Aussa</a>. 16th century also marked the arrival of the Ottomans, who began making inroads in the Red Sea area.<sup id="cite_ref-MB01_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MB01-70">[70]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Pankhurstteb_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pankhurstteb-72">[72]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Aesna_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Aesna-73">[73]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Ottomans had succeeded in conquering the northeastern present-day Eritrea for the next two decades, an area which stretched from <a href="/wiki/Massawa" title="Massawa">Massawa</a> to <a href="/wiki/Suakin" title="Suakin">Swakin</a> in Sudan.<sup id="cite_ref-MB01_70-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MB01-70">[70]</a></sup> The territory became an Ottoman governorate, known as the <a href="/wiki/Habesh_Eyalet" title="Habesh Eyalet">Habesh Eyalet</a>. Massawa served as the new province's first capital. When the city became of secondary economical importance, the administrative capital was soon moved across the Red Sea to <a href="/wiki/Jeddah" title="Jeddah">Jeddah</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-encaet_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-encaet-75">[75]</a></sup> Turks tried to occupy the highland parts of Medri Bahri in 1559 and withdrew after they encountered resistance and were pushed back by the Bahri Negash and highland forces. In 1578 they tried to expand into the highlands with the help of Bahri Negash Yisehaq, who had switched alliances due to a power struggle. But they were defeated and enslaved by Emperor <a href="/wiki/Sarsa_Dengel" title="Sarsa Dengel">Sarsa the great</a> and by 1589, they started raiding the Eritrean population for cattle and slaves but they suffered defeat again and upon the call for protection by the Eritreans, Sarsa punished the Ottomans by sacking their fort at Arqiqo. The Ottomans were eventually driven out in the last quarter of the 16th century. However, they retained control over the seaboard until the establishment of Italian Eritrea in the late 1800s.<sup id="cite_ref-MB01_70-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MB01-70">[70]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-A10-4_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A10-4-76">[76]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-A10-5_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A10-5-77">[77]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_history">Modern history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Modern history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Italian_Eritrea">Italian Eritrea</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Italian Eritrea">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Italian_Eritrea" title="Italian Eritrea">Italian Eritrea</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Eritrea_1896.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Eritrea_1896.jpg/280px-Eritrea_1896.jpg" decoding="async" width="280" height="239" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Eritrea_1896.jpg/420px-Eritrea_1896.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Eritrea_1896.jpg/560px-Eritrea_1896.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1148" data-file-height="978"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Eritrea_1896.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Map of Eritrea in 1896
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The boundaries of the present-day Eritrea nation state were established during the <a href="/wiki/Scramble_for_Africa" title="Scramble for Africa">Scramble for Africa</a>. In 1869<sup id="cite_ref-Ully_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ully-78">[78]</a></sup> or 1870, the ruling local chief sold lands surrounding the Bay of <a href="/wiki/Assab" title="Assab">Assab</a> to the Rubattino Shipping Company.<sup id="cite_ref-EBAb_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EBAb-79">[79]</a></sup> The area served as a <a href="/wiki/Coaling_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Coaling station">coaling station</a> along the <a href="/wiki/Shipping_lane" class="mw-redirect" title="Shipping lane">shipping lanes</a> introduced by the recently completed <a href="/wiki/Suez_Canal" title="Suez Canal">Suez Canal</a>. </p>
      <p>In the vacuum that followed the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Gallabat" title="Battle of Gallabat">1889 death</a> of <a href="/wiki/Emperor_of_Ethiopia" title="Emperor of Ethiopia">Emperor</a> <a href="/wiki/Yohannes_IV" title="Yohannes IV">Yohannes&nbsp;IV</a>, Gen.â<a href="/wiki/Oreste_Baratieri" title="Oreste Baratieri">Oreste Baratieri</a> occupied the highlands along the Eritrean coast and Italy proclaimed the establishment of the new colony of <a href="/wiki/Italian_Eritrea" title="Italian Eritrea">Italian Eritrea</a>, a colony of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Italy" title="Kingdom of Italy">Kingdom of Italy</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Wuchale" title="Treaty of Wuchale">Treaty of Wuchale</a> (It.&nbsp;<i>Uccialli</i>) signed the same year, <a href="/wiki/Menelik_II" title="Menelik II">King Menelik</a> of <a href="/wiki/Shewa" title="Shewa">Shewa</a>, a southern Ethiopian kingdom, recognized the Italian occupation of his rivals' lands of <a href="/wiki/Bogos" class="mw-redirect" title="Bogos">Bogos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hamasien" title="Hamasien">Hamasien</a>, <a href="/wiki/Akkele_Guzay" class="mw-redirect" title="Akkele Guzay">Akkele Guzay</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Serae" title="Serae">Serae</a> in exchange for guarantees of financial assistance and continuing access to European arms and ammunition. His subsequent victory over his rival kings and enthronement as <a href="/wiki/Emperor_of_Ethiopia" title="Emperor of Ethiopia">Emperor</a> <a href="/wiki/Menelik_II_of_Ethiopia" class="mw-redirect" title="Menelik II of Ethiopia">Menelek&nbsp;II</a> (r.&nbsp;1889â1913) made the treaty formally binding upon the entire territory.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1888, the Italian administration launched its first development projects in the new colony. The <a href="/wiki/Eritrean_Railway" title="Eritrean Railway">Eritrean Railway</a> was completed to Saati in 1888,<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> and reached <a href="/wiki/Asmara" title="Asmara">Asmara</a> in the highlands in 1911.<sup id="cite_ref-f1_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-f1-82">[82]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Asmara-Massawa_Cableway" title="Asmara-Massawa Cableway">AsmaraâMassawa Cableway</a> was the longest line in the world during its time, but was later dismantled by the British in World War II. Besides major infrastructural projects, the colonial authorities invested significantly in the agricultural sector. It also oversaw the provision of urban amenities in Asmara and Massawa, and employed many Eritreans in public service, particularly in the police and public works departments.<sup id="cite_ref-f1_82-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-f1-82">[82]</a></sup> Thousands of Eritreans were concurrently enlisted in the army, serving during the <a href="/wiki/Italo-Turkish_War" title="Italo-Turkish War">Italo-Turkish War</a> in Libya as well as the <a href="/wiki/First_Italo-Ethiopian_War" title="First Italo-Ethiopian War">First</a> and <a href="/wiki/Second_Italo-Ethiopian_War" title="Second Italo-Ethiopian War">Second</a> Italo-Abyssinian Wars. </p>
      <p>Additionally, the Italian Eritrea administration opened a number of new factories, which produced buttons, cooking oil, pasta, construction materials, packing meat, tobacco, hide, and other household commodities. In 1939, there were around 2,198 factories and most of the employees were Eritrean citizens. The establishment of industries also made an increase in the number of both Italians and Eritreans residing in the cities. The number of Italians residing in the territory increased from 4,600 to 75,000 in five years; and with the involvement of Eritreans in the industries, trade and fruit plantation was expanded across the nation, while some of the plantations were owned by Eritreans.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1922, <a href="/wiki/Benito_Mussolini" title="Benito Mussolini">Benito Mussolini</a>'s rise to power in Italy brought profound changes to the colonial government in Italian Eritrea. After <i><a href="/wiki/Il_Duce" class="mw-redirect" title="Il Duce">il Duce</a></i> declared the birth of the <a href="/wiki/Italian_Empire" title="Italian Empire">Italian Empire</a> in May 1936, Italian Eritrea (enlarged with northern Ethiopia's regions) and <a href="/wiki/Italian_Somaliland" title="Italian Somaliland">Italian Somaliland</a> were merged with the just conquered Ethiopia in the new <a href="/wiki/Italian_East_Africa" title="Italian East Africa">Italian East Africa</a> (<i>Africa Orientale Italiana</i>) administrative territory. This <a href="/wiki/Fascists" class="mw-redirect" title="Fascists">Fascist</a> period was characterized by imperial expansion in the name of a "new Roman Empire". Eritrea was chosen by the Italian government to be the industrial center of Italian East Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Asmara's architecture after 1935 was greatly improved to become a "modernist Art Deco city" (in 2017 has been declared a "UNESCO World City Heritage"<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup>), featuring <i>eclectic and rationalist built forms, well-defined open spaces, and public and private buildings, including cinemas, shops, banks, religious structures, public and private offices, industrial facilities, and residences</i> (according to UNESCO's publications). The Italians designed more than 400 buildings in a construction boom that was only halted by Italy's involvement in <a href="/wiki/WW2" class="mw-redirect" title="WW2">WW2</a>. These included art deco masterpieces like the worldwide famous <a href="/wiki/Fiat_Tagliero_Building" title="Fiat Tagliero Building">Fiat Tagliero Building</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Cinema_Impero" title="Cinema Impero">Cinema Impero</a><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="British_administration">British administration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: British administration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>Through the 1941 <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Keren" title="Battle of Keren">Battle of Keren</a>, the British expelled the Italians,<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> and took over the administration of the country. </p>
      <p>The British placed Eritrea under British military administration until <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Allied forces</a> could determine its fate. </p>
      <p>In the absence of agreement amongst the Allies concerning the status of Eritrea, British administration continued for the remainder of World War II and until 1950. During the immediate postwar years, the British proposed that Eritrea be divided along religious lines and annexed partly to the British colony of Sudan and partly to Ethiopia.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>, anticipating a <a href="/wiki/Communist" class="mw-redirect" title="Communist">communist</a> victory in the Italian polls, initially supported returning Eritrea to Italy under trusteeship or as a colony.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Federation_with_Ethiopia">Federation with Ethiopia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Federation with Ethiopia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Federation_of_Ethiopia_and_Eritrea" title="Federation of Ethiopia and Eritrea">Federation of Ethiopia and Eritrea</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Eritrean_Independence_War_Map.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Eritrean_Independence_War_Map.png/220px-Eritrean_Independence_War_Map.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="181" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Eritrean_Independence_War_Map.png/330px-Eritrean_Independence_War_Map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Eritrean_Independence_War_Map.png/440px-Eritrean_Independence_War_Map.png 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1642"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Eritrean_Independence_War_Map.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Eritrean_War_of_Independence" title="Eritrean War of Independence">Eritrean War of Independence</a> against Ethiopia 1961â1991
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In the 1950s, the Ethiopian feudal administration under Emperor <a href="/wiki/Haile_Selassie_of_Ethiopia" class="mw-redirect" title="Haile Selassie of Ethiopia">Haile Selassie</a> sought to annex Eritrea and Italian Somaliland. He laid claim to both territories in a letter to Franklin D. Roosevelt at the Paris Peace Conference and at the First Session of the United Nations.<sup id="cite_ref-un_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-un-88">[88]</a></sup> In the United Nations, the debate over the fate of the former Italian colonies continued. The British and Americans preferred to cede all of Eritrea except the Western province to the Ethiopians as a reward for their support during <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> The Independence Bloc of Eritrean parties consistently requested from the UN General Assembly that a referendum be held immediately to settle the Eritrean question of sovereignty. </p>
      <p>Following the adoption of <a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_Resolution_390" class="extiw" title="s:United Nations General Assembly Resolution 390">UN Resolution 390A(V)</a> in December 1950, Eritrea was <a href="/wiki/Federation" title="Federation">federated</a> with Ethiopia under the prompting of the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-UNGA390_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNGA390-90">[90]</a></sup> The resolution called for Eritrea and Ethiopia to be linked through a loose federal structure under the sovereignty of the Emperor. Eritrea was to have its own administrative and judicial structure, its own flag, and control over its domestic affairs, including police, local administration, and taxation.<sup id="cite_ref-un_88-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-un-88">[88]</a></sup> The federal government, which for all practical purposes was the existing imperial government, was to control foreign affairs (including commerce), defense, finance, and transportation. The resolution ignored the wishes of Eritreans for independence, but guaranteed the population democratic rights and a measure of autonomy. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence">Independence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Independence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Eritrean_War_of_Independence" title="Eritrean War of Independence">Eritrean War of Independence</a> and <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Eritrea" title="Flag of Eritrea">Flag of Eritrea</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Asmara_panorama,_Eritrea.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Asmara_panorama%2C_Eritrea.jpg/220px-Asmara_panorama%2C_Eritrea.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Asmara_panorama%2C_Eritrea.jpg/330px-Asmara_panorama%2C_Eritrea.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Asmara_panorama%2C_Eritrea.jpg/440px-Asmara_panorama%2C_Eritrea.jpg 2x" data-file-width="709" data-file-height="471"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Asmara_panorama,_Eritrea.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A view over <a href="/wiki/Asmara" title="Asmara">Asmara</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In 1958, a group of Eritreans founded the Eritrean Liberation Movement (ELM). The organization mainly consisted of Eritrean students, professionals and intellectuals. It engaged in clandestine political activities intended to cultivate resistance to the centralizing policies of the imperial Ethiopian state.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> On 1 September 1961, the <a href="/wiki/Eritrean_Liberation_Front" title="Eritrean Liberation Front">Eritrean Liberation Front</a> (ELF), under the leadership of <a href="/wiki/Hamid_Idris_Awate" title="Hamid Idris Awate">Hamid Idris Awate</a>, waged an armed struggle for independence. In 1962, Emperor <a href="/wiki/Haile_Selassie" title="Haile Selassie">Haile Selassie</a> unilaterally dissolved the Eritrean parliament and <a href="/wiki/Annexation" title="Annexation">annexed</a> the territory. The ensuing <a href="/wiki/Eritrean_War_of_Independence" title="Eritrean War of Independence">Eritrean War of Independence</a> went on for 30 years against successive Ethiopian governments until 1991, when the <a href="/wiki/Eritrean_People%27s_Liberation_Front" title="Eritrean People's Liberation Front">Eritrean People's Liberation Front</a> (EPLF), a successor of the <a href="/wiki/Eritrean_Liberation_Front" title="Eritrean Liberation Front">ELF</a>, defeated the Ethiopian forces in Eritrea and helped a coalition of <a href="/wiki/Ethiopian_People%27s_Revolutionary_Democratic_Front" title="Ethiopian People's Revolutionary Democratic Front">Ethiopian rebel forces</a> take control of the Ethiopian capital <a href="/wiki/Addis_Ababa" title="Addis Ababa">Addis Ababa</a>. </p>
      <p>Following a UN-supervised <a href="/wiki/Eritrean_independence_referendum,_1993" class="mw-redirect" title="Eritrean independence referendum, 1993">referendum in Eritrea</a> (dubbed <a href="/wiki/UNOVER" class="mw-redirect" title="UNOVER">UNOVER</a>) in which the Eritrean people overwhelmingly voted for independence, Eritrea declared its independence and gained international recognition in 1993.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> The EPLF seized power, established a one-party state along nationalist lines and banned further political activity. There have been no elections since. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Un-eritrea.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Un-eritrea.png/300px-Un-eritrea.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="223" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Un-eritrea.png/450px-Un-eritrea.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Un-eritrea.png/600px-Un-eritrea.png 2x" data-file-width="3038" data-file-height="2257"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Un-eritrea.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Map of Eritrea
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Eritrea" title="Geography of Eritrea">Geography of Eritrea</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Location_and_habitat">Location and habitat</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Location and habitat">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Eritrea is located in <a href="/wiki/East_Africa" title="East Africa">East Africa</a>. It is bordered to the northeast and east by the <a href="/wiki/Red_Sea" title="Red Sea">Red Sea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a> to the west, <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a> to the south, and <a href="/wiki/Djibouti" title="Djibouti">Djibouti</a> to the southeast. Eritrea lies between latitudes <a href="/wiki/12th_parallel_north" title="12th parallel north">12Â°</a> and <a href="/wiki/18th_parallel_north" title="18th parallel north">18Â°N</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/36th_meridian_east" title="36th meridian east">36Â°</a> and <a href="/wiki/44th_meridian_east" title="44th meridian east">44Â°E</a>. </p>
      <p>The country is virtually bisected by a branch of the <a href="/wiki/East_African_Rift" title="East African Rift">East African Rift</a>. Eritrea, at the southern end of the Red Sea, is the home of the fork in the rift. The <a href="/wiki/Dahlak_Archipelago" title="Dahlak Archipelago">Dahlak Archipelago</a> and its fishing grounds are situated off the sandy and arid coastline. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Dahlak_reliefmap.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Dahlak_reliefmap.png/220px-Dahlak_reliefmap.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="229" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Dahlak_reliefmap.png/330px-Dahlak_reliefmap.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Dahlak_reliefmap.png/440px-Dahlak_reliefmap.png 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="3120"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Dahlak_reliefmap.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Dahlak_Archipelago" title="Dahlak Archipelago">Dahlak Archipelago</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Eritrea can be split into three <a href="/wiki/Ecoregion" title="Ecoregion">ecoregions</a>. To the east of the highlands are the hot, arid coastal plains stretching down to the southeast of the country. The cooler, more fertile highlands, reaching up to 3000 m, have a different habitat. Habitats here vary from the <a href="/wiki/Tropical_and_subtropical_moist_broadleaf_forests" title="Tropical and subtropical moist broadleaf forests">sub-tropical rainforest</a> at Filfil Solomona to the precipitous cliffs and <a href="/wiki/Canyon" title="Canyon">canyons</a> of the southern highlands.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Afar_Triangle" title="Afar Triangle">Afar Triangle</a> or Danakil Depression of Eritrea is the probable location of a <a href="/wiki/Triple_junction" title="Triple junction">triple junction</a> where three tectonic plates are pulling away from one another. The highest point of the country, <a href="/wiki/Emba_Soira" title="Emba Soira">Emba Soira</a>, is located in the center of Eritrea, at 3,018 meters (9,902&nbsp;ft) <a href="/wiki/Above_mean_sea_level" class="mw-redirect" title="Above mean sea level">above sea level</a>. </p>
      <p>The main cities of the country are the capital city of <a href="/wiki/Asmara" title="Asmara">Asmara</a> and the port town of <a href="/wiki/Asseb" class="mw-redirect" title="Asseb">Asseb</a> in the southeast, as well as the towns of <a href="/wiki/Massawa" title="Massawa">Massawa</a> to the east, the northern town of <a href="/wiki/Keren,_Eritrea" title="Keren, Eritrea">Keren</a>, and the central town <a href="/wiki/Mendefera" title="Mendefera">Mendefera</a>. </p>
      <p>Eritrea is part of a 14-nation constituency within the <a href="/wiki/Global_Environment_Facility" title="Global Environment Facility">Global Environment Facility</a>, which partners with international institutions, civil society organizations, and the private sector to address global environmental issues while supporting national sustainable development initiatives.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> Local variability in rainfall patterns and/or reduced precipitation is known to occur, which may precipitate soil erosion, floods, droughts, <a href="/wiki/Land_degradation" title="Land degradation">land degradation</a> and desertification.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> In 2006, Eritrea also announced that it would become the first country in the world to turn its entire coast into an environmentally protected zone. The 1,347&nbsp;km (837&nbsp;mi) coastline, along with another 1,946&nbsp;km (1,209&nbsp;mi) of coast around its more than 350 islands, will come under governmental protection. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto;overflow:hidden;width:auto;max-width:808px">
       <div class="thumbinner">
        <div class="noresize" style="overflow:auto">
         <a href="/wiki/File:2006-11-01_Asmara-Massawa_01.jpg" class="image" title="Highlands between Asmara and Massawa"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/2006-11-01_Asmara-Massawa_01.jpg/800px-2006-11-01_Asmara-Massawa_01.jpg" decoding="async" width="800" height="244" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/2006-11-01_Asmara-Massawa_01.jpg/1200px-2006-11-01_Asmara-Massawa_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/2006-11-01_Asmara-Massawa_01.jpg/1600px-2006-11-01_Asmara-Massawa_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4522" data-file-height="1382"></a>
        </div>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="text-align:center">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:2006-11-01_Asmara-Massawa_01.jpg" title="File:2006-11-01 Asmara-Massawa 01.jpg"> </a>
         </div>Highlands between <a href="/wiki/Asmara" title="Asmara">Asmara</a> and <a href="/wiki/Massawa" title="Massawa">Massawa</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wildlife">Wildlife</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Wildlife">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Eritrea" title="Wildlife of Eritrea">Wildlife of Eritrea</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_mammals_in_Eritrea" class="mw-redirect" title="List of mammals in Eritrea">List of mammals in Eritrea</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_birds_of_Eritrea" title="List of birds of Eritrea">List of birds of Eritrea</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Eritrean_birds_-_pelicans_in_Asmara_pound.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Eritrean_birds_-_pelicans_in_Asmara_pound.jpg/220px-Eritrean_birds_-_pelicans_in_Asmara_pound.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Eritrean_birds_-_pelicans_in_Asmara_pound.jpg/330px-Eritrean_birds_-_pelicans_in_Asmara_pound.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Eritrean_birds_-_pelicans_in_Asmara_pound.jpg/440px-Eritrean_birds_-_pelicans_in_Asmara_pound.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="683"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Eritrean_birds_-_pelicans_in_Asmara_pound.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Pelicans" class="mw-redirect" title="Pelicans">Pelicans</a> in a pond near <a href="/wiki/Asmara" title="Asmara">Asmara</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Eritrea has several species of mammals and a rich avifauna of 560 species of birds.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Eritrea is home to an abundant amount of big game species. Enforced regulations have helped in steadily increasing their numbers throughout Eritrea.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> Mammals commonly seen today include the <a href="/wiki/Abyssinian_hare" title="Abyssinian hare">Abyssinian hare</a>, <a href="/wiki/African_wild_cat" class="mw-redirect" title="African wild cat">African wild cat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Black-backed_jackal" title="Black-backed jackal">Black-backed jackal</a>, <a href="/wiki/African_golden_wolf" title="African golden wolf">African golden wolf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Genet_(animal)" title="Genet (animal)">Genet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ground_squirrel" title="Ground squirrel">Ground squirrel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pale_fox" title="Pale fox">pale fox</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soemmerring%27s_gazelle" title="Soemmerring's gazelle">Soemmerring's gazelle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Warthog" title="Warthog">warthog</a>. <a href="/wiki/Dorcas_gazelle" title="Dorcas gazelle">Dorcas gazelle</a> are common on the coastal plains and in <a href="/wiki/Gash-Barka_Region" title="Gash-Barka Region">Gash-Barka</a>. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Eri_landscape.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Eri_landscape.jpg/220px-Eri_landscape.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Eri_landscape.jpg/330px-Eri_landscape.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Eri_landscape.jpg/440px-Eri_landscape.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="683"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Eri_landscape.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Eritrean landscape near road to Massawa
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Lions" class="mw-redirect" title="Lions">Lions</a> are said to inhabit the mountains of the Gash-Barka Region. There is also a small population of <a href="/wiki/African_bush_elephant" title="African bush elephant">African bush elephants</a> that roam in some parts of the country. <a href="/wiki/Dik-diks" class="mw-redirect" title="Dik-diks">Dik-diks</a> can also be found in many areas. The endangered <a href="/wiki/African_wild_ass" title="African wild ass">African wild ass</a> can be seen in Denakalia Region. Other local wildlife include <a href="/wiki/Bushbuck" class="mw-redirect" title="Bushbuck">bushbuck</a>, <a href="/wiki/Duikers" class="mw-redirect" title="Duikers">duikers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greater_kudu" title="Greater kudu">greater kudu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Klipspringer" title="Klipspringer">Klipspringer</a>, <a href="/wiki/African_leopards" class="mw-redirect" title="African leopards">African leopards</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oryx" title="Oryx">oryx</a> and <a href="/wiki/Crocodiles" class="mw-redirect" title="Crocodiles">crocodiles</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ibis.atwebpages.com_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ibis.atwebpages.com-99">[99]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Spotted_hyena" title="Spotted hyena">spotted hyena</a> is widespread and fairly common. Between 1955 and 2001 there were no reported sightings of elephant herds, and they are thought to have fallen victim to the war of independence. In December 2001 a herd of about 30, including 10 juveniles, was observed in the vicinity of the <a href="/wiki/Gash_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Gash River">Gash River</a>. The elephants seemed to have formed a <a href="/wiki/Symbiosis" title="Symbiosis">symbiotic</a> relationship with <a href="/wiki/Olive_baboon" title="Olive baboon">olive baboons</a>, with the baboons using the water holes dug by the elephants, while the elephants use the tree-top baboons as an early warning system. </p>
      <p>It is estimated that there are around 100 <a href="/wiki/Elephants" class="mw-redirect" title="Elephants">African bush elephant</a> left in Eritrea, the most northerly of East Africa's elephants.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Endangered" class="mw-redirect" title="Endangered">endangered</a> <a href="/wiki/African_wild_dog" title="African wild dog">African wild dog</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Lycaon_pictus" class="mw-redirect" title="Lycaon pictus">Lycaon pictus</a></i>) was previously found in Eritrea, but is now deemed extirpated from the entire country.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> In Gash-Barka, snakes like <a href="/wiki/Echis_pyramidum" title="Echis pyramidum">saw-scaled viper</a> are common. <a href="/wiki/Bitis_arietans" class="mw-redirect" title="Bitis arietans">Puff adder</a> and <a href="/wiki/Red_spitting_cobra" title="Red spitting cobra">red spitting cobra</a> are widespread and can be found even in the highlands. In the coastal areas marine species that are common include <a href="/wiki/Dolphin" title="Dolphin">dolphin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dugong" title="Dugong">dugong</a>, <a href="/wiki/Whale_shark" title="Whale shark">whale shark</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turtles" class="mw-redirect" title="Turtles">turtles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marlin" title="Marlin">marlin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Swordfish" title="Swordfish">swordfish</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Manta_ray" title="Manta ray">manta ray</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ibis.atwebpages.com_99-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ibis.atwebpages.com-99">[99]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Based on variations in temperature, Eritrea can be broadly divided into three major climate zones: the <a href="/wiki/Temperate_zone" class="mw-redirect" title="Temperate zone">temperate zone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate">subtropical climate zone</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tropical_climate_zone" class="mw-redirect" title="Tropical climate zone">tropical climate zone</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> The climate of Eritrea is shaped by its diverse topographical features and its location within the tropics. The diversity in landscape and topography in the highlands and lowlands of Eritrea result in the diversity of climate across the country. The highlands have temperate climate throughout the year. The climate of most lowland zones is arid and semiarid. The distribution of rainfall and vegetation types varies markedly throughout the country. Eritrean climate varies on the basis of seasonal and altitudinal differences. </p>
