      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Government and politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Eritrea" title="Politics of Eritrea">Politics of Eritrea</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:162px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:National_Assembly_of_Eritrea.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/National_Assembly_of_Eritrea.svg/160px-National_Assembly_of_Eritrea.svg.png" decoding="async" width="160" height="82" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/National_Assembly_of_Eritrea.svg/240px-National_Assembly_of_Eritrea.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/National_Assembly_of_Eritrea.svg/320px-National_Assembly_of_Eritrea.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="360" data-file-height="185"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:National_Assembly_of_Eritrea.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The National Assembly of Eritrea
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Front_for_Democracy_and_Justice" title="People's Front for Democracy and Justice">People's Front for Democracy and Justice</a> (PFDJ) is the <a href="/wiki/One-party_state" title="One-party state">only legal party</a> in Eritrea.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-104">[104]</a></sup> Other political groups are not allowed to organize, although the unimplemented <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Eritrea" title="Constitution of Eritrea">Constitution of 1997</a> provides for the existence of <a href="/wiki/Multi-party_system" title="Multi-party system">multi-party politics</a>. The National Assembly has 150 seats. National elections have been periodically scheduled and cancelled; none have ever been held in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-21">[21]</a></sup> President <a href="/wiki/Isaias_Afwerki" title="Isaias Afwerki">Isaias Afwerki</a> has been in office since independence in 1993. In 1993, 75 representatives were elected to the National Assembly; the rest are appointed. As the report by the UN Human Rights Council explained: "No national elections have taken place since that time, and no presidential elections have ever taken place. Local or regional elections have not been held since 2003â2004.The National Assembly elected independent Eritreaâs first president, Isaias Afwerki, in 1993. Following his election, Afwerki consolidated his control of the Eritrean government." President Isaias Afwerki has regularly expressed his disdain for what he refers to as "western-style" democracy. In a 2008 interview with Al Jazeera, for example, the President stated that "Eritrea will wait three or four decades, maybe more, before it holds elections. Who knows?"<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="National_elections">National elections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: National elections">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_Eritrea" title="Elections in Eritrea">Elections in Eritrea</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Given that the full implementation of the Joint Declaration of Peace and Friendship between Eritrea and Ethiopia is still incomplete, the Eritrean authorities still do not consider that peace agreement is formally implemented. However, local elections have continued in Eritrea. The most recent round of local government elections were held in 2010 and 2011. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Eritrean_Defence_Forces" title="Eritrean Defence Forces">Eritrean Defence Forces</a> are now the official <a href="/wiki/Armed_forces" class="mw-redirect" title="Armed forces">armed forces</a> of the State of Eritrea. Eritrea's military is one of the largest in Africa. </p>
      <p>Compulsory military service was instituted in 1995. Officially, conscripts, male and female, must serve for 18 months minimum, which includes six months of military training and 12 months doing the regular school year to complete their last year of high school. Thus around 5% of Eritreans live in barracks in the desert doing projects such as road building as part of their service </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Defense.gov_News_Photo_021210-D-2987S-057.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Defense.gov_News_Photo_021210-D-2987S-057.jpg/220px-Defense.gov_News_Photo_021210-D-2987S-057.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Defense.gov_News_Photo_021210-D-2987S-057.jpg/330px-Defense.gov_News_Photo_021210-D-2987S-057.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Defense.gov_News_Photo_021210-D-2987S-057.jpg/440px-Defense.gov_News_Photo_021210-D-2987S-057.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2690" data-file-height="1920"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Defense.gov_News_Photo_021210-D-2987S-057.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>President <a href="/wiki/Isaias_Afewerki" class="mw-redirect" title="Isaias Afewerki">Isaias Afewerki</a> with U.S. Secretary of Defense <a href="/wiki/Donald_Rumsfeld" title="Donald Rumsfeld">Donald Rumsfeld</a>, December 2002
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The National Service Proclamation of 1995 does not recognize the right to conscientious objection to military service. According to the 1957 Ethiopian penal code adopted by Eritrea during independence, failure to enlist in the military or refusal to perform military service are punishable with imprisonment terms of six months to five years and up to ten years, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> National service enlistment times may be extended during times of "national crisis"; since 1998, everyone under the age of 50 is enlisted in national service for an indefinite period until released, which may depend on the arbitrary decision of a commander. In a study of 200 escaped conscripts, the average service was 6.5 years, and some had served more than 12 years.<sup id="cite_ref-National_service_in_Eritrea_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-National_service_in_Eritrea-107">[107]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_profession">Legal profession</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Legal profession">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>According to the NYU School of Law, the Legal Committee of the Ministry of Justice oversees the admission and requirements to practice law in Eritrea. Although the establishment of an independent bar association is not proscribed under Proclamation 88/96, among other domestic laws, there is no bar association. The community electorate in the local jurisdiction of the Community Court chooses the Court's judges. The Community Court's standing on women in the legal profession is unclear, but elected women judges have reserved seat.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Eritrea" title="Foreign relations of Eritrea">Foreign relations of Eritrea</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Eritrea is a member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, the <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a>, and is an <a href="/wiki/Arab%E2%80%93Eritrean_relations" title="ArabâEritrean relations">observing member</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Arab_League" title="Arab League">Arab League</a> alongside <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a> and <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-edition.cnn.com_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-edition.cnn.com-28">[28]</a></sup> The nation holds a seat on the United Nations' Advisory Committee on Administrative and Budgetary Questions (ACABQ). Eritrea also holds memberships in the <a href="/wiki/International_Bank_for_Reconstruction_and_Development" title="International Bank for Reconstruction and Development">International Bank for Reconstruction and Development</a>, <a href="/wiki/International_Finance_Corporation" title="International Finance Corporation">International Finance Corporation</a>, <a href="/wiki/International_Criminal_Police_Organization" class="mw-redirect" title="International Criminal Police Organization">International Criminal Police Organization</a> (INTERPOL), <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">Non-Aligned Movement</a>, <a href="/wiki/Organisation_for_the_Prohibition_of_Chemical_Weapons" title="Organisation for the Prohibition of Chemical Weapons">Organisation for the Prohibition of Chemical Weapons</a>, <a href="/wiki/Permanent_Court_of_Arbitration" title="Permanent Court of Arbitration">Permanent Court of Arbitration</a>, <a href="/wiki/Port_Management_Association_of_Eastern_and_Southern_Africa" title="Port Management Association of Eastern and Southern Africa">Port Management Association of Eastern and Southern Africa</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/World_Customs_Organization" title="World Customs Organization">World Customs Organization</a>. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:The_23d_ICSOE_Conference_for_East_Africa_in_Asmara,_Eritrea_2019.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/The_23d_ICSOE_Conference_for_East_Africa_in_Asmara%2C_Eritrea_2019.png/260px-The_23d_ICSOE_Conference_for_East_Africa_in_Asmara%2C_Eritrea_2019.png" decoding="async" width="260" height="169" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/The_23d_ICSOE_Conference_for_East_Africa_in_Asmara%2C_Eritrea_2019.png/390px-The_23d_ICSOE_Conference_for_East_Africa_in_Asmara%2C_Eritrea_2019.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/The_23d_ICSOE_Conference_for_East_Africa_in_Asmara%2C_Eritrea_2019.png/520px-The_23d_ICSOE_Conference_for_East_Africa_in_Asmara%2C_Eritrea_2019.png 2x" data-file-width="1123" data-file-height="732"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:The_23d_ICSOE_Conference_for_East_Africa_in_Asmara,_Eritrea_2019.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The 23d ISCOE <a href="/wiki/East_Africa" title="East Africa">East Africa</a> Conference in <a href="/wiki/Asmara" title="Asmara">Asmara</a> in 2019
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Eritrean government previously withdrew its representative to the African Union to protest the AU's alleged lack of leadership in facilitating the implementation of a binding border decision demarcating the border between Eritrea and Ethiopia. The Eritrean government has since January 2011 appointed an envoy, Tesfa-Alem Tekle, to the AU.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Eritrea maintains diplomatic ties with a number of other countries: it has over 31 <a href="/wiki/Embassy" class="mw-redirect" title="Embassy">embasies</a> and <a href="/wiki/Consulate" title="Consulate">consulates</a> abroad, and over 22 consulates and embassies representated in the country,<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> including <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China%E2%80%93Eritrea_relations" class="mw-redirect" title="People's Republic of ChinaâEritrea relations">China</a>, <a href="/wiki/Denmark%E2%80%93Eritrea_relations" title="DenmarkâEritrea relations">Denmark</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia-Eritrea_relations" class="mw-redirect" title="Ethiopia-Eritrea relations">Ethiopia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Djibouti%E2%80%93Eritrea_relations" title="DjiboutiâEritrea relations">Djibouti</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eritrea%E2%80%93Israel_relations" title="EritreaâIsrael relations">Israel</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Eritrea%E2%80%93United_States_relations" title="EritreaâUnited States relations">United States</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eritrea%E2%80%93Yemen_relations" title="EritreaâYemen relations">Yemen</a>. Its relations with Djibouti and Yemen are tense due to territorial disputes over the <a href="/wiki/Doumeira_Islands" title="Doumeira Islands">Doumeira Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hanish_Islands" title="Hanish Islands">Hanish Islands</a>, respectively. </p>
      <p>On 28 May 2019, the United States removed Eritrea from the "Counterterror Non-Cooperation List" which also includes: <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> Moreover, Eritrea was visited two months earlier by a US congressional delegation for the first time in 14 years.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Relations_with_Ethiopia">Relations with Ethiopia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Relations with Ethiopia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Eritrea%E2%80%93Ethiopia_relations" title="EritreaâEthiopia relations">EritreaâEthiopia relations</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eritrean%E2%80%93Ethiopian_War" title="EritreanâEthiopian War">EritreanâEthiopian War</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Eritrean_War_of_Independence" title="Eritrean War of Independence">Eritrean War of Independence</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eritrean_independence_referendum,_1993" class="mw-redirect" title="Eritrean independence referendum, 1993">Eritrean independence referendum, 1993</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Independence_Day_of_Eritrea.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Independence_Day_of_Eritrea.jpg/220px-Independence_Day_of_Eritrea.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Independence_Day_of_Eritrea.jpg/330px-Independence_Day_of_Eritrea.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Independence_Day_of_Eritrea.jpg/440px-Independence_Day_of_Eritrea.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4928" data-file-height="3264"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Independence_Day_of_Eritrea.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Independence_Day_(Eritrea)" title="Independence Day (Eritrea)">Independence Day of Eritrea</a> is one of the most important public holidays in the country.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The undemarcated border with Ethiopia is the primary external issue currently facing Eritrea. Eritrea's relations with Ethiopia turned from that of cautious mutual tolerance, following the 30-year war for Eritrean independence, to a deadly rivalry that led to the outbreak of hostilities from May 1998 to June 2000 which claimed approximately 70,000 lives from both sides.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> The border conflict cost hundreds of millions of dollars.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Disagreements following the war have resulted in stalemate punctuated by periods of elevated tension and renewed threats of war.<sup id="cite_ref-horntension1_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-horntension1-115">[115]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-horntension3_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-horntension3-117">[117]</a></sup> The stalemate led the President of Eritrea to urge the UN to take action on Ethiopia with the <a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Eleven_Letters" class="extiw" title="s:Eleven Letters">Eleven Letters</a> penned by the President to the United Nations Security Council. The situation has been further escalated by the continued efforts of the Eritrean and Ethiopian leaders in supporting opposition in one another's countries.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In 2011, Ethiopia accused Eritrea of planting bombs at an <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a> summit in <a href="/wiki/Addis_Ababa" title="Addis Ababa">Addis Ababa</a>, which was later supported by a UN report. Eritrea denied the claims.<sup id="cite_ref-aubomb_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aubomb-118">[118]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A peace treaty between both nations was signed on 8 July 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> The next day, they signed a joint declaration formally ending the <a href="/wiki/Eritrean%E2%80%93Ethiopian_border_conflict" title="EritreanâEthiopian border conflict">EritreanâEthiopian border conflict</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Eritrea" title="Regions of Eritrea">Regions of Eritrea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Eritrea" class="mw-redirect" title="Districts of Eritrea">Districts of Eritrea</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Eritrea is divided into six administrative <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Eritrea" title="Regions of Eritrea">regions</a>. These areas are further divided into 58 <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Eritrea" class="mw-redirect" title="Districts of Eritrea">districts</a>. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Eritrea,_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Eritrea%2C_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored.svg/290px-Eritrea%2C_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored.svg.png" decoding="async" width="290" height="238" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Eritrea%2C_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored.svg/435px-Eritrea%2C_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Eritrea%2C_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored.svg/580px-Eritrea%2C_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1844" data-file-height="1514"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Eritrea,_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A map of Eritrea regions. 1.Northern Red Sea, 2.Anseba, 3.Gash-Barka, 4.Central(to right), 5.Southern, 6.Southern Red Sea
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>

         <td>1,300 </td> 
         <td>1,053,254 </td> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Asmara" title="Asmara">Asmara</a> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Anseba_Region" title="Anseba Region">Anseba</a> </td> 
         <td>23,200 </td> 
         <td>893,587 </td> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Keren,_Eritrea" title="Keren, Eritrea">Keren</a> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Gash-Barka_Region" title="Gash-Barka Region">Gash-Barka</a> </td> 
         <td>33,200 </td> 
         <td>1,103,742 </td> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Barentu,_Eritrea" title="Barentu, Eritrea">Barentu</a> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Southern_Region_(Eritrea)" title="Southern Region (Eritrea)">Southern</a> </td> 
         <td>8,000 </td> 
         <td>1,476,765 </td> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Mendefera" title="Mendefera">Mendefera</a> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Northern_Red_Sea_Region" title="Northern Red Sea Region">Northern Red Sea</a> </td> 
         <td>27,800 </td> 
         <td>897,454 </td> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Massawa" title="Massawa">Massawa</a> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Southern_Red_Sea_Region" title="Southern Red Sea Region">Southern Red Sea</a> </td> 
         <td>27,600 </td> 
         <td>398,073 </td> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Assab" title="Assab">Assab</a> </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p><br> The regions of Eritrea are the primary geographical divisions through which the country is administered. Six in total, they include the Maekel/Central, Anseba, Gash-Barka, Debub/Southern, Northern Red Sea and Southern Red Sea regions. At the time of independence in 1993, Eritrea was arranged into ten provinces. These provinces were similar to the nine provinces operating during the colonial period. In 1996, these were consolidated into six regions (zobas). The boundaries of these new regions are based on catchment basins. </p> 
      <div style="clear:both;"></div>

      <p>Asmara is the capital city of Eritrea with a population of 898,000 people. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Eritrean_mountai_road_archietcture.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Eritrean_mountai_road_archietcture.jpg/250px-Eritrean_mountai_road_archietcture.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Eritrean_mountai_road_archietcture.jpg/375px-Eritrean_mountai_road_archietcture.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Eritrean_mountai_road_archietcture.jpg/500px-Eritrean_mountai_road_archietcture.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="683"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Eritrean_mountai_road_archietcture.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Eritrean mountain road
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Eritrea" title="Transport in Eritrea">Transport in Eritrea</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Transport in Eritrea includes highways, airports, railway, and seaports in addition to various forms of public and private vehicular, maritime and aerial transportation. </p>
      <p>The Eritrean highway system is named according to the road classification. The three levels of classification are: primary (P), secondary (S), and tertiary (T). The lowest level road is tertiary and serves local interests. Typically they are improved earth roads which are occasionally paved. During the wet seasons these roads typically become impassable. </p>
      <p>The next higher level road is a secondary road and typically is a single-layered asphalt road that connects district capitals together and those to the regional capitals. Roads that are considered primary roads are those that are fully asphalted (throughout their entire length) and in general they carry traffic between all the major cities and towns in Eritrea. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Train_Asmara_Eritrea.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Train_Asmara_Eritrea.jpg/260px-Train_Asmara_Eritrea.jpg" decoding="async" width="260" height="173" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Train_Asmara_Eritrea.jpg/390px-Train_Asmara_Eritrea.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Train_Asmara_Eritrea.jpg/520px-Train_Asmara_Eritrea.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1166" data-file-height="778"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Train_Asmara_Eritrea.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Steam train outside <a href="/wiki/Asmara" title="Asmara">Asmara</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Eritrean_Railway" title="Eritrean Railway">Eritrean Railway</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>As of 1999, there is a total of 317 kilometres of <span class="nowrap">950&nbsp;mm</span> (<span class="nowrap">3&nbsp;ft&nbsp;<span class="frac">1<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r993651011">.mw-parser-output .sr-only{border:0;clip:rect(0,0,0,0);height:1px;margin:-1px;overflow:hidden;padding:0;position:absolute;width:1px;white-space:nowrap}</style><span class="sr-only">&nbsp;</span><sup>3</sup>â<sub>8</sub></span>&nbsp;in</span>) (narrow gauge) rail line in Eritrea. The <a href="/wiki/Eritrean_Railway" title="Eritrean Railway">Eritrean Railway</a> was built between 1887 and 1932.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> Badly damaged during <a href="/wiki/WWII" class="mw-redirect" title="WWII">WWII</a> and in later fighting, it was closed section by section, with the final closure coming in 1978.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> After independence, a rebuilding effort commenced, and the first rebuilt section was reopened in 2003. As of 2009, the section from <a href="/wiki/Massawa" title="Massawa">Massawa</a> to <a href="/wiki/Asmara" title="Asmara">Asmara</a> was fully rebuilt and available for service. </p>
      <p>Rehabilitation of the remainder and of the rolling stock has occurred in recent years. Current service is very limited due to the extreme age of most of the railway equipment and its limited availability. Further rebuilding is planned. The railway linking Agordat and Asmara with the port of Massawa; had been inoperative since 1978 except for about a 5 kilometre stretch that was reopened in Massawa in 1994. A railway formerly ran from Massawa to Bishia via Asmara, and is under re-construction. </p>
      <p>Even during the war, Eritrea developed its <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Eritrea" title="Transport in Eritrea">transportation infrastructure</a> by asphalting new roads, improving its ports, and repairing war-damaged roads and bridges as a part of the <a href="/wiki/Wefri_Warsay_Yika%27alo" title="Wefri Warsay Yika'alo">Wefri Warsay Yika'alo</a> program. The most significant of these projects was the construction of a coastal highway of more than 500&nbsp;km connecting <a href="/wiki/Massawa" title="Massawa">Massawa</a> with <a href="/wiki/Asseb" class="mw-redirect" title="Asseb">Asseb</a>, as well as the rehabilitation of the <a href="/wiki/Eritrean_Railway" title="Eritrean Railway">Eritrean Railway</a>. The rail line has been restored between the port of Massawa and the capital Asmara, although services are sporadic. Steam locomotives are sometimes used for groups of enthusiasts. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Eritrea" title="Economy of Eritrea">Economy of Eritrea</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:En_visualize_explore_tree_map_hs92_export_eri_all_show_2013_(4).png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/En_visualize_explore_tree_map_hs92_export_eri_all_show_2013_%284%29.png/330px-En_visualize_explore_tree_map_hs92_export_eri_all_show_2013_%284%29.png" decoding="async" width="330" height="97" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/En_visualize_explore_tree_map_hs92_export_eri_all_show_2013_%284%29.png/495px-En_visualize_explore_tree_map_hs92_export_eri_all_show_2013_%284%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/En_visualize_explore_tree_map_hs92_export_eri_all_show_2013_%284%29.png/660px-En_visualize_explore_tree_map_hs92_export_eri_all_show_2013_%284%29.png 2x" data-file-width="1317" data-file-height="388"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:En_visualize_explore_tree_map_hs92_export_eri_all_show_2013_(4).png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Eritrea's main exports, 2013
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The economy of Eritrea has experienced considerable growth in recent years (2010â20), indicated by an annual improvement in gross domestic product (GDP) with over 5% in recent years, some years up to 8.7%.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> A big reason for the recent growth of the Eritrean economy is the commencement of full operations in the gold and silver Bisha mine and the production of cement from the cement factory in Massawa.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The economy of Eritrea has also bounced back after a period of minor or negative growth, indicated by an improvement in the Real Gross Domestic Product (Real GDP) to 12% in 2018 after averaging -2.7% for some time between 2015â18.<sup id="cite_ref-Eritrea_World_Bank_2019_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eritrea_World_Bank_2019-127">[127]</a></sup> A major contributor to the recovery is investment in Eritrea's <a href="/wiki/Copper" title="Copper">copper</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zinc" title="Zinc">zinc</a>, and Colluli potash mining operations from Australian<sup id="cite_ref-Mining_Technology_2019_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mining_Technology_2019-128">[128]</a></sup> and Chinese<sup id="cite_ref-Bloomberg_2018_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bloomberg_2018-129">[129]</a></sup> mining companies. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Eritrean_Airlines_Boeing_767-300ER_E3-AAO_FCO_2005-6-7.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Eritrean_Airlines_Boeing_767-300ER_E3-AAO_FCO_2005-6-7.png/220px-Eritrean_Airlines_Boeing_767-300ER_E3-AAO_FCO_2005-6-7.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Eritrean_Airlines_Boeing_767-300ER_E3-AAO_FCO_2005-6-7.png/330px-Eritrean_Airlines_Boeing_767-300ER_E3-AAO_FCO_2005-6-7.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Eritrean_Airlines_Boeing_767-300ER_E3-AAO_FCO_2005-6-7.png/440px-Eritrean_Airlines_Boeing_767-300ER_E3-AAO_FCO_2005-6-7.png 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="890"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Eritrean_Airlines_Boeing_767-300ER_E3-AAO_FCO_2005-6-7.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>An <a href="/wiki/Eritrean_Airlines" title="Eritrean Airlines">Eritrean Airlines</a> Boeing 767-366/ER aircraft. The national carrier is based in <a href="/wiki/Asmara" title="Asmara">Asmara</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p> The real GDP (2020 est.): $8.1&nbsp;billion, and the annual growth rate (2020 est.) about:6%. The GDP PPP (2020 est.): $11.3&nbsp;billion<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Worker <a href="/wiki/Remittance" title="Remittance">remittances</a> from abroad are estimated to account for 32% of gross domestic product.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-19">[19]</a></sup> Eritrea has an extensive amount of resources such as copper, gold, granite, marble, and potash. The Eritrean economy has undergone extreme changes due to the War of Independence. In 2011, Eritrea's GDP grew by 8.7% making it one of the fastest-growing economies in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>70% of the Eritrean workforce <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_Eritrea" title="Agriculture in Eritrea">are employed in agriculture</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-huffingtonpost.com_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-huffingtonpost.com-132">[132]</a></sup> accounting for roughly one-third of the economy.<sup id="cite_ref-Eritrea_World_Bank_2019_127-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eritrea_World_Bank_2019-127">[127]</a></sup> Eritrea's main agricultural products include <a href="/wiki/Sorghum" title="Sorghum">sorghum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Millet" title="Millet">millet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barley" title="Barley">barley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wheat" title="Wheat">wheat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Legume" title="Legume">legumes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vegetable" title="Vegetable">vegetables</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fruit" title="Fruit">fruits</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sesame" title="Sesame">sesame</a>, <a href="/wiki/Linseed" class="mw-redirect" title="Linseed">linseed</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cattle" title="Cattle">cattle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sheep" title="Sheep">sheep</a>, <a href="/wiki/Goats" class="mw-redirect" title="Goats">goats</a> and <a href="/wiki/Camels" class="mw-redirect" title="Camels">camels</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Eritrean%E2%80%93Ethiopian_War" title="EritreanâEthiopian War">EritreanâEthiopian War</a> severely hurt Eritrea's economy. <a href="/wiki/Gross_Domestic_Product" class="mw-redirect" title="Gross Domestic Product">GDP</a> growth in 1999 fell to less than 1%, and GDP decreased by 8.2% in 2000. In May 2000, the war resulted in some $600&nbsp;million in property damage and loss, including losses of $225&nbsp;million in <a href="/wiki/Livestock" title="Livestock">livestock</a> and 55,000 homes. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Eritrea" title="Tourism in Eritrea">Tourism in Eritrea</a> makes up less than 1% of the GDP. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Traditional_Eritrean_dance.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Traditional_Eritrean_dance.jpg/170px-Traditional_Eritrean_dance.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="287" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Traditional_Eritrean_dance.jpg/255px-Traditional_Eritrean_dance.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Traditional_Eritrean_dance.jpg/340px-Traditional_Eritrean_dance.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1211" data-file-height="2048"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Traditional_Eritrean_dance.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A traditional Eritrean dance in traditional clothing
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Barentu2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Barentu2.jpg/220px-Barentu2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="108" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Barentu2.jpg/330px-Barentu2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Barentu2.jpg/440px-Barentu2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="246"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Barentu2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A man and a woman in <a href="/wiki/Barentu,_Eritrea" title="Barentu, Eritrea">Barentu</a> in traditional clothes
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Eritrea" title="Demographics of Eritrea">Demographics of Eritrea</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Eritrea's population increased from 3.2&nbsp;million to approximately 5,755,124<sup id="cite_ref-cia_factbook_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia_factbook-12">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Eritrea_population_(2020)_live_Countrymeters_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eritrea_population_(2020)_live_Countrymeters-13">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-statista.com_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-statista.com-14">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-indexmundi.com_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-indexmundi.com-15">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-who.int_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-who.int-16">[16]</a></sup> between 1990 and 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-Eritrea_population_(2020)_live_Countrymeters_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eritrea_population_(2020)_live_Countrymeters-13">[13]</a></sup> The average number of children born to Eritrean mothers is 4.1. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_composition">Ethnic composition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Ethnic composition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>There are nine recognized ethnic groups according to the government of Eritrea.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_21-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-21">[21]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> An independent census has yet to be conducted, but the <a href="/wiki/Tigrayans" title="Tigrayans">Tigrinya people</a> make up about 55% and <a href="/wiki/Tigre_people" title="Tigre people">Tigre people</a> make up about 30% of the population. A majority of the remaining ethnic groups belong to <a href="/wiki/Afroasiatic_languages" title="Afroasiatic languages">Afroasiatic</a>-speaking communities of the <a href="/wiki/Cushitic_languages" title="Cushitic languages">Cushitic</a> branch, such as the <a href="/wiki/Saho_people" title="Saho people">Saho</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hedareb_people" title="Hedareb people">Hedareb</a>, <a href="/wiki/Afar_people" title="Afar people">Afar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bilen_people" title="Bilen people">Bilen</a>. There are also a number of <a href="/wiki/Nilotic_peoples" title="Nilotic peoples">Nilotic</a> ethnic groups, who are represented in Eritrea by the <a href="/wiki/Kunama_people" title="Kunama people">Kunama</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nara_people" title="Nara people">Nara</a>. Each ethnicity speaks a different native tongue but, typically, many of the minorities speak more than one language. The <a href="/wiki/Rashaida_people" title="Rashaida people">Rashaida</a> represent about 2% of Eritrea's population.<sup id="cite_ref-Ciaethn_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ciaethn-5">[5]</a></sup> They reside in the northern coastal lowlands of Eritrea as well as the eastern coasts of Sudan. The Rashaida first came to Eritrea in the 19th century from the <a href="/wiki/Hejaz" title="Hejaz">Hejaz</a> region.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In addition, there exist <a href="/wiki/Italian_Eritreans" title="Italian Eritreans">Italian Eritrean</a> (concentrated in Asmara) and Ethiopian Tigrayan communities. Neither is generally given citizenship unless through marriage or, more rarely, by having it conferred upon them by the State. Eritrea had about 760,000 inhabitants, including 70,000 Italians, in 1941.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> Most Italians left after Eritrea became independent from Italy. It is estimated up to 100,000 Eritreans are of Italian descent.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Eritrea" title="Languages of Eritrea">Languages of Eritrea</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Population_pyramid_of_Eritrea_2016.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Population_pyramid_of_Eritrea_2016.png/220px-Population_pyramid_of_Eritrea_2016.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Population_pyramid_of_Eritrea_2016.png/330px-Population_pyramid_of_Eritrea_2016.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Population_pyramid_of_Eritrea_2016.png/440px-Population_pyramid_of_Eritrea_2016.png 2x" data-file-width="610" data-file-height="425"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Population_pyramid_of_Eritrea_2016.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Population pyramid of Eritrea 2016
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Eritrea is a multilingual country. The nation has no official language, as the Constitution establishes the "equality of all Eritrean languages".<sup id="cite_ref-auto3_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto3-1">[1]</a></sup> Eritrea has nine national languages which are <a href="/wiki/Tigrinya_language" title="Tigrinya language">Tigrinya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tigre_language" title="Tigre language">Tigre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Afar_language" title="Afar language">Afar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beja_language" title="Beja language">Beja</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bilen_language" title="Bilen language">Bilen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kunama_language" title="Kunama language">Kunama</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nara_language" title="Nara language">Nara</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Saho_language" title="Saho language">Saho</a>. Tigrinya, <a href="/wiki/Arabic" title="Arabic">Arabic</a>, and <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> serve as de facto working languages, with English used in university education and many technical fields. While <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a>, the former colonial language, holds no government recognized status in Eritrea, it is spoken by a few monolinguals and Asmara has <a href="/wiki/Istituto_Italiano_Statale_Omnicomprensivo_di_Asmara" title="Istituto Italiano Statale Omnicomprensivo di Asmara">Scuola Italiana di Asmara</a>, a long running Italian government-operated school.<sup id="cite_ref-Ethner_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ethner-139">[139]</a></sup> Also, native Eritreans assimilated the language of the Italian Eritreans and spoke a version of Italian mixed with many Tigrinya words: <a href="/wiki/Eritrean_Italian" class="mw-redirect" title="Eritrean Italian">Eritrean Italian</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tigrinya_language" title="Tigrinya language">Tigrinya</a> serves as the de facto language of national identity. With 2,540,000 total speakers of a population of 5,254,000 in 2006, it is the most widely spoken language, particularly in the southern and central parts of Eritrea. </p>
      <p>Most of the languages spoken in Eritrea belong to the <a href="/wiki/Ethiopian_Semitic_languages" title="Ethiopian Semitic languages">Ethiopian Semitic</a> branch of the <a href="/wiki/Afroasiatic_languages" title="Afroasiatic languages">Afroasiatic</a> family.<sup id="cite_ref-Minahan_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Minahan-141">[141]</a></sup> Other Afroasiatic languages belonging to the <a href="/wiki/Cushitic_languages" title="Cushitic languages">Cushitic</a> branch are also widely spoken in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-Minahan_141-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Minahan-141">[141]</a></sup> The latter include <a href="/wiki/Afar_language" title="Afar language">Afar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beja_language" title="Beja language">Beja</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blin_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Blin language">Blin</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Saho_language" title="Saho language">Saho</a>. In addition, <a href="/wiki/Nilo-Saharan_languages" title="Nilo-Saharan languages">Nilo-Saharan languages</a> (<a href="/wiki/Kunama_language" title="Kunama language">Kunama</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nara_language" title="Nara language">Nara</a>) are spoken as a <a href="/wiki/Native_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Native language">native language</a> by the Nilotic Kunama and Nara ethnic groups that live in the western and northwestern part of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-Minahan_141-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Minahan-141">[141]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Smaller groups also speak other Afroasiatic languages, such as the newly recognized <a href="/wiki/Dahlik_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Dahlik language">Dahlik</a> and Arabic (the <a href="/wiki/Hejazi_Arabic" title="Hejazi Arabic">Hejazi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hadhrami_Arabic" title="Hadhrami Arabic">Hadhrami</a> <a href="/wiki/Varieties_of_Arabic" title="Varieties of Arabic">dialects</a> spoken by the Rashaida and Hadhrami, respectively). </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Eritrea" title="Religion in Eritrea">Religion in Eritrea</a>
