      <p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Pew_Research_Center" title="Pew Research Center">Pew Research Center</a>, as of 2010<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, 62.9% of the population of Eritrea adheres to <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a>, 36.6% follows <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>, and 0.4% practices <a href="/wiki/Traditional_African_religions" title="Traditional African religions">folk religion</a>. The remainder observes <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Judaism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a> and other faiths (&lt;0.1% each), or are religiously unaffiliated (0.1%).<sup id="cite_ref-Pew_143-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pew-143">[143]</a></sup> The U.S. Department of State estimates that, as of 2011<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, 50% of the population of Eritrea adheres to Christianity, 48% follows Islam, and 2% observes other religions, including traditional faiths and animism.<sup id="cite_ref-webcitation.org_142-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-webcitation.org-142">[142]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> is the oldest world religion practiced in the country, and the first Christian monastery <a href="/wiki/Debre_Sina_(monastery)" title="Debre Sina (monastery)">Debre Sina (monastery)</a> was built during the 4th century. <sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Since May 2002, the government of Eritrea has officially recognized the <a href="/wiki/Eritrean_Orthodox_Tewahedo_Church" title="Eritrean Orthodox Tewahedo Church">Eritrean Orthodox Tewahedo Church</a> (<a href="/wiki/Oriental_Orthodox" class="mw-redirect" title="Oriental Orthodox">Oriental Orthodox</a>), <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam" title="Sunni Islam">Sunni Islam</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Eritrean_Catholic_Church" title="Eritrean Catholic Church">Eritrean Catholic Church</a> (a <a href="/wiki/Metropolis_(religious_jurisdiction)" title="Metropolis (religious jurisdiction)">Metropolitanate</a> sui juris), and the <a href="/wiki/Evangelical" class="mw-redirect" title="Evangelical">Evangelical</a> <a href="/wiki/Lutheranism" title="Lutheranism">Lutheran</a> church. All other faiths and denominations are required to undergo a registration process.<sup id="cite_ref-Religious_persecution_in_Eritrea_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Religious_persecution_in_Eritrea-145">[145]</a></sup> Among other things, the government's registration system requires religious groups to submit personal information on their membership to be allowed to <a href="/wiki/Worship" title="Worship">worship</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Religious_persecution_in_Eritrea_145-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Religious_persecution_in_Eritrea-145">[145]</a></sup> </p> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r989373448">@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery{width:100%!important}}.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery{display:table}.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery-default{background:transparent;margin-top:.3em}.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery-center{margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto}.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery-left{float:left}.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery-right{float:right}.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery-none{float:none}.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery-collapsible{width:100%}.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery .title,.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery .main,.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery .footer{display:table-row}.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery .title>div{display:table-cell;text-align:center;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery .main>div{display:table-cell}.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery .gallery{line-height:1.35em}.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery .footer>div{display:table-cell;text-align:right;font-size:80%;line-height:1em}.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery .title>div *,.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery .footer>div *{overflow:visible}.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery .gallerybox img{background:none!important}.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery .bordered-images .thumb img{border:solid #eaecf0 1px}.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery .whitebg .thumb{background:#fff!important}</style>
      <div class="mod-gallery mod-gallery-default mod-gallery-right">
       <div class="main">
        <div>
         <ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional nochecker bordered-images whitebg"> 
          <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 235px">
           <div style="width: 235px"> 
            <div class="thumb" style="width: 230px;">
             <div style="margin:25px auto;">
              <a href="/wiki/File:Sheikh_Hanafi_Mosque_(8529064326).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Sheikh_Hanafi_Mosque_%288529064326%29.jpg/200px-Sheikh_Hanafi_Mosque_%288529064326%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Sheikh_Hanafi_Mosque_%288529064326%29.jpg/300px-Sheikh_Hanafi_Mosque_%288529064326%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Sheikh_Hanafi_Mosque_%288529064326%29.jpg/400px-Sheikh_Hanafi_Mosque_%288529064326%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768"></a>
             </div>
            </div> 
            <div class="gallerytext"> 
             <p>The 15th century Sheikh Hanafi Mosque in <a href="/wiki/Massawa" title="Massawa">Massawa</a> </p> 
            </div> 
           </div></li> 
          <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 235px">
           <div style="width: 235px"> 
            <div class="thumb" style="width: 230px;">
             <div style="margin:33.5px auto;">
              <a href="/wiki/File:Asmara,_cattedrale_cattolica,_01.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Asmara%2C_cattedrale_cattolica%2C_01.JPG/200px-Asmara%2C_cattedrale_cattolica%2C_01.JPG" decoding="async" width="200" height="133" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Asmara%2C_cattedrale_cattolica%2C_01.JPG/300px-Asmara%2C_cattedrale_cattolica%2C_01.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Asmara%2C_cattedrale_cattolica%2C_01.JPG/400px-Asmara%2C_cattedrale_cattolica%2C_01.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="2304"></a>
             </div>
            </div> 
            <div class="gallerytext"> 
             <p><a href="/wiki/Church_of_Our_Lady_of_the_Rosary,_Asmara" title="Church of Our Lady of the Rosary, Asmara">Church of Our Lady of the Rosary</a> in the capital <a href="/wiki/Asmara" title="Asmara">Asmara</a> </p> 
            </div> 
           </div></li> 
         </ul>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Eritrean government is against what it deems as "reformed" or "radical" versions of its established religions. Therefore, alleged radical forms of Islam and Christianity, <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah's Witnesses">Jehovah's Witnesses</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%CA%BC%C3%AD_Faith" title="BahÃ¡Ê¼Ã­ Faith">BahÃ¡Ê¼Ã­ Faith</a> (though the BahÃ¡Ê¼Ã­ Faith is neither Islamic nor Christian), the <a href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventist_Church" title="Seventh-day Adventist Church">Seventh-day Adventist Church</a>, and numerous other non-<a href="/wiki/Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant">Protestant</a> Evangelical denominations are not registered and cannot worship freely. Three named Jehovah's Witnesses are known to have been imprisoned since 1994 along with 51 others.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup> The government treats Jehovah's Witnesses especially harshly, denying them ration cards and work permits.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> Jehovah's Witnesses were stripped of their citizenship and basic civil rights by presidential decree in October 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In its 2017 religious freedom report, the U.S. State Department named Eritrea a Country of Particular Concern (CPC).<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="UNESCO_World_Heritage_Site">UNESCO World Heritage Site</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: UNESCO World Heritage Site">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>On 8 July 2017, the entire capital city of <a href="/wiki/Asmara" title="Asmara">Asmara</a> was listed as a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO_World_Heritage_Site" class="mw-redirect" title="UNESCO World Heritage Site">UNESCO World Heritage Site</a>, with the inscription taking place during the 41st World Heritage Committee Session. </p>
      <p>The city has thousands of <a href="/wiki/Art_Deco#Architecture" title="Art Deco">Art Deco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Futurist" title="Futurist">futurist</a>, <a href="/wiki/Modernist" class="mw-redirect" title="Modernist">modernist</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rationalism_(architecture)" title="Rationalism (architecture)">rationalist</a> buildings, constructed during the period of <a href="/wiki/Italian_Eritrea" title="Italian Eritrea">Italian Eritrea</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-auto1_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-152">[152]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup> Asmara, a small town in the nineteenth century, started to grow quickly during 1889.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup> The city also became a place "to experiment with radical new designs", mainly futuristic and art deco inspired.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> Even though city planners, architects, and engineers were largely European, members of the indigenous population were largely used as construction workers, Asmarinos still identify with their cityâs legacy.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup> </p> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;max-width:242px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:119px;max-width:119px">
          <div class="thumbimage" style="height:175px;overflow:hidden">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Asmara,_museo_nazionale,_ingresso.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Asmara%2C_museo_nazionale%2C_ingresso.JPG/117px-Asmara%2C_museo_nazionale%2C_ingresso.JPG" decoding="async" width="117" height="176" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Asmara%2C_museo_nazionale%2C_ingresso.JPG/176px-Asmara%2C_museo_nazionale%2C_ingresso.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Asmara%2C_museo_nazionale%2C_ingresso.JPG/234px-Asmara%2C_museo_nazionale%2C_ingresso.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2304" data-file-height="3456"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           <a href="/wiki/National_Museum_of_Eritrea" title="National Museum of Eritrea">Eritrean national museum</a> in Asmara
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:119px;max-width:119px">
          <div class="thumbimage" style="height:175px;overflow:hidden">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Fiat_tagliero,_07,0.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Fiat_tagliero%2C_07%2C0.JPG/117px-Fiat_tagliero%2C_07%2C0.JPG" decoding="async" width="117" height="176" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Fiat_tagliero%2C_07%2C0.JPG/176px-Fiat_tagliero%2C_07%2C0.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Fiat_tagliero%2C_07%2C0.JPG/234px-Fiat_tagliero%2C_07%2C0.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2304" data-file-height="3456"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           <a href="/wiki/Fiat_Tagliero_Building" title="Fiat Tagliero Building">The Fiat Tagliero Building</a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The city shows off most early 20th-century architectural styles. Some buildings are <a href="/wiki/Neo-Romanesque_architecture" class="mw-redirect" title="Neo-Romanesque architecture">neo-Romanesque</a>, such as the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Our_Lady_of_the_Rosary,_Asmara" title="Church of Our Lady of the Rosary, Asmara">Church of Our Lady of the Rosary</a>. Art Deco influences are found throughout the city. Essences of <a href="/wiki/Cubism" title="Cubism">Cubism</a> can be found on the Africa Pension Building, and on a small collection of buildings. The <a href="/wiki/Fiat_Tagliero_Building" title="Fiat Tagliero Building">Fiat Tagliero Building</a> shows almost the height of futurism, just as it was coming into big fashion in Italy. In recent times, some buildings have been functionally built which sometimes can spoil the atmosphere of some cities, but they fit into Asmara as it is such a modern city. </p>
      <p>Many buildings such as opera houses, hotels, and cinemas where built during this period. Some notable buildings include the <a href="/wiki/Art_Deco" title="Art Deco">Art Deco</a> <a href="/wiki/Cinema_Impero" title="Cinema Impero">Cinema Impero</a> (opened in 1937 and considered by the experts one of the world's finest examples of Art DÃ©co style building<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup>), Cubist Africa Pension, eclectic Eritrean Orthodox <a href="/wiki/Enda_Mariam_Cathedral,_Asmara" title="Enda Mariam Cathedral, Asmara">Enda Mariam Cathedral</a> and <a href="/wiki/Asmara_Theatre" title="Asmara Theatre">Asmara Opera</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Futurist_architecture" title="Futurist architecture">futurist</a> <a href="/wiki/Fiat_Tagliero_Building" title="Fiat Tagliero Building">Fiat Tagliero Building</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Neoclassical_architecture" title="Neoclassical architecture">neoclassical</a> <a href="/wiki/Governor%27s_Palace_(Asmara)" class="mw-redirect" title="Governor's Palace (Asmara)">Asmara city hall</a>. </p>
      <p>A statement from UNESCO read: </p> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r996844942">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style>
      <blockquote class="templatequote">
       <p>It is an exceptional example of early modernist urbanism at the beginning of the 20th century and its application in an African context.</p>
       <div class="templatequotecite">
        ââ<cite><a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a><sup id="cite_ref-auto1_152-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-152">[152]</a></sup></cite>
       </div>
      </blockquote> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Human rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Eritrea" title="Human rights in Eritrea">Human rights in Eritrea</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Eritrea_-_Government_building,_Asmara.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Eritrea_-_Government_building%2C_Asmara.jpg/220px-Eritrea_-_Government_building%2C_Asmara.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Eritrea_-_Government_building%2C_Asmara.jpg/330px-Eritrea_-_Government_building%2C_Asmara.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Eritrea_-_Government_building%2C_Asmara.jpg/440px-Eritrea_-_Government_building%2C_Asmara.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1278" data-file-height="847"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Eritrea_-_Government_building,_Asmara.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Building of regional administration in <a href="/wiki/Asmara" title="Asmara">Asmara</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Eritrea is a <a href="/wiki/One-party_state" title="One-party state">one-party state</a> in which national legislative elections have been repeatedly postponed.<sup id="cite_ref-gi_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gi-25">[25]</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a>, the government's <a href="/wiki/Human_rights" title="Human rights">human rights</a> record is considered among the worst in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-hrw_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hrw-26">[26]</a></sup> Most countries have accused the Eritrean authorities of <a href="/wiki/Arbitrary_arrest_and_detention" title="Arbitrary arrest and detention">arbitrary arrest and detentions</a>, and of detaining an unknown number of people without charge for their political activism. Both male and female <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Eritrea" title="LGBT rights in Eritrea">same-sex sexual activity</a> is illegal in Eritrea.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A prominent group of fifteen Eritreans, called the G-15, including three cabinet members, were arrested in September 2001 after publishing an open letter to the government and President Isaias Afewerki calling for democratic dialogue. This group and thousands of others who were alleged to be affiliated with them are imprisoned without legal charges, hearing, trial and judgment.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-163">[163]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Eritrean_G-15_advocacy_site_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eritrean_G-15_advocacy_site-164">[164]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Since Eritrea's conflict with Ethiopia in 1998â2001, the nation's human rights record has been criticized at the United Nations.<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian-165">[165]</a></sup> Human rights violations are allegedly often committed by the government or on behalf of the government. <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_speech" title="Freedom of speech">Freedom of speech</a>, <a href="/wiki/News_media" title="News media">press</a>, <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_assembly" title="Freedom of assembly">assembly</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Interpersonal_relationship" title="Interpersonal relationship">association</a> are limited. Those who practice "unregistered" religions, try to flee the nation, or escape military duty are arrested and put into <a href="/wiki/Prison" title="Prison">prison</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian_165-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian-165">[165]</a></sup> During the Eritrean independence struggle and 1998 <a href="/wiki/Eritrean-Ethiopian_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Eritrean-Ethiopian War">Eritrean-Ethiopian War</a>, many atrocities were also committed by the Ethiopian authorities against unarmed Eritrean civilians.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Asmara,_mai_jah_jah_02.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Asmara%2C_mai_jah_jah_02.JPG/220px-Asmara%2C_mai_jah_jah_02.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Asmara%2C_mai_jah_jah_02.JPG/330px-Asmara%2C_mai_jah_jah_02.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Asmara%2C_mai_jah_jah_02.JPG/440px-Asmara%2C_mai_jah_jah_02.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="2304"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Asmara,_mai_jah_jah_02.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Asmara" title="Asmara">Asmara</a>, Eritrea in 2015
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Gash_Barkahouses.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Gash_Barkahouses.jpg/220px-Gash_Barkahouses.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="88" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Gash_Barkahouses.jpg/330px-Gash_Barkahouses.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Gash_Barkahouses.jpg/440px-Gash_Barkahouses.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="200"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Gash_Barkahouses.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Traditional Eritrean agudo/tukul huts in a village near <a href="/wiki/Barentu,_Eritrea" title="Barentu, Eritrea">Barentu</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In June 2016, a 500-page <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Human_Rights_Council" title="United Nations Human Rights Council">United Nations Human Rights Council</a> report accused Eritrea's government of extrajudicial executions, torture, indefinitely prolonged national service (6.5 years on average) and forced labour, and indicated that sexual harassment, rape and sexual servitude by state officials are also widespread.<sup id="cite_ref-UNHRC_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNHRC-7">[7]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-guard_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guard-168">[168]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Lochbihler" title="Barbara Lochbihler">Barbara Lochbihler</a> of the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament_Subcommittee_on_Human_Rights" title="European Parliament Subcommittee on Human Rights">European Parliament Subcommittee on Human Rights</a> said the report detailed 'very serious human rights violations', and asserted that EU funding for development would not continue as at present without change in Eritrea.<sup id="cite_ref-DWelle_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DWelle-169">[169]</a></sup> The Eritrean Foreign Ministry responded by describing the commission's report as "wild allegations" which were "totally unfounded and devoid of all merit".<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup> Several countries also disputed the report's language and accuracy, including the US and China.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>All Eritreans aged between 18 and 40 years must complete a mandatory national service, which includes military service. This requirement was implemented after Eritrea gained <a href="/wiki/Independence" title="Independence">independence</a> from Ethiopia, as a means to protect Eritrea's <a href="/wiki/Sovereignty" title="Sovereignty">sovereignty</a>, to instill national pride, and to create a disciplined populace.<sup id="cite_ref-National_service_in_Eritrea_107-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-National_service_in_Eritrea-107">[107]</a></sup> Eritrea's national service requires long, indefinite conscription (6.5 years on average), which some Eritreans leave the country in order to avoid.<sup id="cite_ref-National_service_in_Eritrea_107-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-National_service_in_Eritrea-107">[107]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In an attempt at reform, Eritrean government officials and NGO representatives in 2006 participated in many public meetings and dialogues. In these sessions they answered questions as fundamental as, "What are human rights?", "Who determines what are human rights?", and "What should take precedence, human or communal rights?"<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup> In 2007, the Eritrean government also banned <a href="/wiki/Female_genital_mutilation" title="Female genital mutilation">female genital mutilation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup> In Regional Assemblies and religious circles, Eritreans themselves speak out continuously against the use of female circumcision. They cite health concerns and individual freedom as being of primary concern when they say this. Furthermore, they implore rural peoples to cast away this ancient cultural practice.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup> In 2009, a movement called Citizens for Democratic Rights in Eritrea formed to create dialogue between the government and political opposition. The group consists of ordinary citizens and some people close to the government.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup> Since the movement's creation, no significant effort has been made by the Eritrean government to improve its record on human rights. </p>
      <p>In July 2019, UN ambassadors of 37 countries, including Eritrea, have signed a joint letter to the <a href="/wiki/UNHRC" class="mw-redirect" title="UNHRC">UNHRC</a> defending China's treatment of <a href="/wiki/Uyghurs" title="Uyghurs">Uyghurs</a> and other Muslim minority groups in the <a href="/wiki/Xinjiang" title="Xinjiang">Xinjiang</a> region.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media_freedom">Media freedom</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Media freedom">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In its 2017 Press Freedom Index, <a href="/wiki/Reporters_Without_Borders" title="Reporters Without Borders">Reporters Without Borders</a> ranked the media environment in Eritrea at the bottom of a list of 180 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a>, "Eritrea is the only African country to have no privately owned news media",<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup> and Reporters Without Borders said of the public media, "[They] do nothing but relay the regime's belligerent and ultra-nationalist discourse. ... Not a single [foreign correspondent] now lives in Asmara."<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup> The state-owned news agency censors news about external events.<sup id="cite_ref-censored_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-censored-183">[183]</a></sup> Independent media have been banned since 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-censored_183-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-censored-183">[183]</a></sup> The Eritrean authorities had reportedly imprisoned the fourth highest number of journalists after <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>, <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> and <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Health_care">Health care</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Health care">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Eritrea" title="Health in Eritrea">Health in Eritrea</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Eritrea has achieved significant improvements in health care and is one of the few countries to be on target to meet its <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Development_Goal" class="mw-redirect" title="Millennium Development Goal">Millennium Development Goals</a> (MDG) for health, in particular child health.<sup id="cite_ref-ODI1_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ODI1-185">[185]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">Life expectancy</a> at birth increased from 39.1 years in 1960 to 66.44 years in 2020;<sup id="cite_ref-auto2_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto2-186">[186]</a></sup> maternal and <a href="/wiki/Child_mortality" title="Child mortality">child mortality</a> rates dropped dramatically and the health infrastructure expanded.<sup id="cite_ref-ODI1_185-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ODI1-185">[185]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organisation</a> (WHO) in 2008 found average life expectancy to be slightly less than 63 years, a number that has increased to 66.44 in 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-auto2_186-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto2-186">[186]</a></sup><a href="/wiki/Immunization" title="Immunization">Immunisation</a> and child nutrition have been tackled by working closely with schools in a multi-sectoral approach; the number of children vaccinated against measles almost doubled in seven years, from 40.7% to 78.5% and the prevalence of underweight children decreased by 12% from 1995 to 2002 (severe underweight prevalence by 28%).<sup id="cite_ref-ODI1_185-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ODI1-185">[185]</a></sup> The National Malaria Protection Unit of the Ministry of Health registered reductions in malarial mortality by as much as 85% and in the number of cases by 92% between 1998 and 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-ODI1_185-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ODI1-185">[185]</a></sup> The Eritrean government has banned <a href="/wiki/Female_genital_mutilation" title="Female genital mutilation">female genital mutilation</a> (FGM), saying the practice was painful and put women at risk of life-threatening health problems.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>However, Eritrea still faces many challenges. Although the number of physicians increased from only 0.2 in 1993 to 0.5 in 2004 per 1000 people, this is still very low.<sup id="cite_ref-ODI1_185-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ODI1-185">[185]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">Malaria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tuberculosis" title="Tuberculosis">tuberculosis</a> are common.<sup id="cite_ref-afro.who.int_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-afro.who.int-188">[188]</a></sup> HIV prevalence for ages 15 to 49 years exceeds 2%.<sup id="cite_ref-afro.who.int_188-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-afro.who.int-188">[188]</a></sup> The fertility rate is about 4.1 births per woman.<sup id="cite_ref-afro.who.int_188-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-afro.who.int-188">[188]</a></sup> Maternal mortality dropped by more than half from 1995 to 2002, but is still high.<sup id="cite_ref-ODI1_185-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ODI1-185">[185]</a></sup> Similarly, the number of births attended by skilled health personnel doubled from 1995 to 2002, but still is only 28.3%.<sup id="cite_ref-ODI1_185-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ODI1-185">[185]</a></sup> A major cause of death in newborns is severe <a href="/wiki/Infection" title="Infection">infection</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-afro.who.int_188-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-afro.who.int-188">[188]</a></sup> Per-capita expenditure on health is low.<sup id="cite_ref-afro.who.int_188-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-afro.who.int-188">[188]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:EritreaInstituteOfTechnology.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/EritreaInstituteOfTechnology.jpg/250px-EritreaInstituteOfTechnology.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="125" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/EritreaInstituteOfTechnology.jpg/375px-EritreaInstituteOfTechnology.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/EritreaInstituteOfTechnology.jpg/500px-EritreaInstituteOfTechnology.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4600" data-file-height="2300"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:EritreaInstituteOfTechnology.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Eritrea_Institute_of_Technology" title="Eritrea Institute of Technology">Eritrea Institute of Technology</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Eritrea" title="Education in Eritrea">Education in Eritrea</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Eritrea_13.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Eritrea_13.jpg/220px-Eritrea_13.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Eritrea_13.jpg/330px-Eritrea_13.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Eritrea_13.jpg/440px-Eritrea_13.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4032" data-file-height="3024"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Eritrea_13.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Eritrean pupils in uniform
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>There are five levels of education in Eritrea: <a href="/wiki/Preschool_education" class="mw-redirect" title="Preschool education">pre-primary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Primary_education" title="Primary education">primary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Middle_school" title="Middle school">middle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Secondary_education" title="Secondary education">secondary</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Higher_education" title="Higher education">post-secondary</a>. There are nearly 1,270,000 students in the primary, middle, and secondary levels of education.<sup id="cite_ref-uis.unesco.org_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uis.unesco.org-189">[189]</a></sup> There are approximately 824 schools,<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup> two universities (the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Asmara" title="University of Asmara">University of Asmara</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Eritrea_Institute_of_Technology" title="Eritrea Institute of Technology">Eritrea Institute of Technology</a>) and several smaller colleges and technical schools. </p>
      <p>Education in Eritrea is officially compulsory for children aged 6 to 13 years.<sup id="cite_ref-uis.unesco.org_189-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uis.unesco.org-189">[189]</a></sup> </p> 
      <table class="wikitable" style="float: center; margin-center: 10px"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th scope="col" style="background:#77B5FE;">Education system in Eritrea<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-191">[191]</a></sup> </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>Basic Education- 7 years </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>Middle - Junior High School (Years included in basic) </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>Secondary -Secondary School - 4 years </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>Post- secondary - Advanced Diploma - 3 years </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>Higher Education - Bachelor - 4/5 years </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>Higher Education - Master - 2 years </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>Statistics vary at the elementary level, suggesting that 70% to 90% of school-aged children attend primary school; Approximately 61% attend secondary school. Student-teacher ratios are high: 45:1 at the elementary level and 54:1 at the secondary level. Class sizes average 63 and 97 students per classroom at the elementary and secondary school levels, respectively. Learning hours at school are often less than six hours per day. </p>
      <p>Barriers to education in Eritrea include traditional <a href="/wiki/Taboos" class="mw-redirect" title="Taboos">taboos</a>, school fees (for registration and materials), and the <a href="/wiki/Opportunity_costs" class="mw-redirect" title="Opportunity costs">opportunity costs</a> of <a href="/wiki/Low-income" class="mw-redirect" title="Low-income">low-income</a> households.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Eritrea_Institute_of_Technology" title="Eritrea Institute of Technology">Eritrea Institute of Technology</a> "EIT" is a technological institute located near the town Himbrti, <a href="/wiki/Mai_Nefhi" title="Mai Nefhi">Mai Nefhi</a> outside <a href="/wiki/Asmara" title="Asmara">Asmara</a>. The institute has three colleges: <a href="/wiki/Science" title="Science">Science</a>, <a href="/wiki/Engineering" title="Engineering">Engineering</a> and <a href="/wiki/Technology" title="Technology">Technology</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Education" title="Education">Education</a>. The institute began with about 5,500 students during the 2003-2004 <a href="/wiki/Academic_year" title="Academic year">academic year</a>. </p> 
      <table class="BarChartTemplate" style="border-style:solid; border-width:1px; border-color:#c0c0c0; background-color:#fdfdfd; text-align:left; float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.5em 1em;" cellpadding="1"> 
       <caption style="font-weight:bold">
        Literacy rate Eritrea 2020, source: World bank, UNESCO<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_191-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-191">[191]</a></sup> 
       </caption> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th scope="col">Literacy rate </th> 
         <th scope="col" style="width: 20em};">Percent (%) </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <th scope="row" style="font-weight:normal;">Whole population </th> 
         <td>
          <div style="height: 1.25em; width: 20em;">
           <div style="position: absolute; background-color: #77B5FE; width:16.8em; height: 1.25em; margin: 0 0 0 0; z-index: 0;"></div><span style="position: absolute; height:1.25em; width: 20em; padding: 0 0 0 2em; z-index: 10;"><span class="nowrap">84</span></span>
          </div> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <th scope="row" style="font-weight:normal;">Age: 15-24 </th> 
         <td>
          <div style="height: 1.25em; width: 20em;">
           <div style="position: absolute; background-color: #77B5FE; width:18.7em; height: 1.25em; margin: 0 0 0 0; z-index: 0;"></div><span style="position: absolute; height:1.25em; width: 20em; padding: 0 0 0 2em; z-index: 10;"><span class="nowrap">93.27</span></span>
          </div> </td>
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>The EIT was opened after the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Asmara" title="University of Asmara">University of Asmara</a> was reorganized. According to the Ministry of Education, the institution was established, as one of many efforts to achieve equal distribution of higher learning in areas outside the capital city, Asmara. Accordingly, several similar colleges are also established in different other parts of the country. The Eritrea Institute of Technology is the main local institute of higher studies in science, engineering and education. The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Asmara" title="University of Asmara">University of Asmara</a> is the oldest University in the country and was opened in 1958.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup> It is currently not in operation. </p>
      <p>The overall literacy rate in Eritrea is 84%.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">[195]</a></sup> However, the literacy rate is higher for ages 18 to 24 years, it is 92.6% for men and 87.7% for women (2008â2012)<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Eritrea" title="Culture of Eritrea">Culture of Eritrea</a>
      </div> 
      <p>One of the most recognizable parts of Eritrean culture is the <a href="/wiki/Coffee_ceremony" title="Coffee ceremony">coffee ceremony</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup> Coffee (<a href="/wiki/Ge%27ez_alphabet" class="mw-redirect" title="Ge'ez alphabet">Ge'ez</a> á¡á <i>bÅ«n</i>) is offered when visiting friends, during festivities, or as a daily staple of life. During the coffee ceremony, there are traditions that are upheld. The coffee is served in three rounds: the first brew or round is called <i>awel</i> in Tigrinya (meaning "first"), the second round is called <i>kalaay</i> (meaning "second"), and the third round is called <i>bereka</i> (meaning "to be blessed"). </p>
      <p>Traditional Eritrean attire is quite varied among the ethnic groups of Eritrea. In the larger cities, most people dress in Western casual dress such as jeans and shirts. In offices, both men and women often dress in suits. A common traditional clothing for <a href="/wiki/Christians" title="Christians">Christian</a> Tigrinya highlanders consists of bright white gowns called <i><a href="/wiki/Zuria" title="Zuria">zurias</a></i> for the women, and a white shirt accompanied by white pants for the men. In Muslim communities in the Eritrean lowland, the women traditionally dress in brightly colored clothes. Besides convergent culinary tastes, Eritreans share an appreciation for similar music and lyrics, jewelry and fragrances, and tapestry and fabrics as many other populations in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-Tekle197_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tekle197-198">[198]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Eritrean_cuisine" title="Eritrean cuisine">Eritrean cuisine</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Eritrean_Injera_with_stews.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Eritrean_Injera_with_stews.jpg/220px-Eritrean_Injera_with_stews.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="138" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Eritrean_Injera_with_stews.jpg/330px-Eritrean_Injera_with_stews.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Eritrean_Injera_with_stews.jpg/440px-Eritrean_Injera_with_stews.jpg 2x" data-file-width="539" data-file-height="338"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Eritrean_Injera_with_stews.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Eritrean <a href="/wiki/Injera" title="Injera">injera</a> with various stews
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>A typical traditional Eritrean dish consists of <a href="/wiki/Injera" title="Injera">injera</a> accompanied by a spicy stew, which frequently includes beef, chicken, lamb or fish.<sup id="cite_ref-Kittler_199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kittler-199">[199]</a></sup> Overall, Eritrean cuisine strongly resembles those of neighboring <a href="/wiki/Ethiopian_cuisine" title="Ethiopian cuisine">Ethiopia</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Kittler_199-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kittler-199">[199]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Tekle142_200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tekle142-200">[200]</a></sup> Eritrean cooking tend to feature more <a href="/wiki/Seafood" title="Seafood">seafood</a> than Ethiopian cuisine on account of their coastal location.<sup id="cite_ref-Kittler_199-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kittler-199">[199]</a></sup> Eritrean dishes are also frequently "lighter" in texture than Ethiopian meals. They likewise tend to employ less <a href="/wiki/Niter_kibbeh" title="Niter kibbeh">seasoned butter</a> and spices and more <a href="/wiki/Tomato" title="Tomato">tomatoes</a>, as in the <i><a href="/wiki/Tsebhi" class="mw-redirect" title="Tsebhi">tsebhi</a> dorho</i> delicacy. </p>
      <p>Additionally, owing to its colonial history, cuisine in Eritrea features more <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italian</a> influences than are present in Ethiopian cooking, including more <a href="/wiki/Pasta" title="Pasta">pasta</a> and greater use of <a href="/wiki/Curry" title="Curry">curry</a> powders and <a href="/wiki/Cumin" title="Cumin">cumin</a>. The Italian Eritrean cuisine started to be practiced during the colonial times of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Italy" title="Kingdom of Italy">Kingdom of Italy</a>, when a large number of Italians moved to Eritrea. They brought the use of pasta to <a href="/wiki/Italian_Eritrea" title="Italian Eritrea">Italian Eritrea</a>, and it is one of the main food eaten in present-day <a href="/wiki/Asmara" title="Asmara">Asmara</a>. An <a href="/wiki/Italian_Eritrean_cuisine" title="Italian Eritrean cuisine">Italian Eritrean cuisine</a> emerged, and common dishes are 'Pasta al Sugo e Berbere', which means "Pasta with tomato sauce and berbere" (spice), but there are many more like <a href="/wiki/Lasagna" class="mw-redirect" title="Lasagna">lasagna</a> and "cotoletta alla milanese" (milano cutlet).<sup id="cite_ref-Mftdbeaeccdtmts_201-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mftdbeaeccdtmts-201">[201]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In addition to coffee, local alcoholic beverages are enjoyed. These include <i>sowa</i>, a bitter drink made from fermented barley, and <i>mies</i>, a fermented honey wine.<sup id="cite_ref-Mettm_202-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mettm-202">[202]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Helen_Meles.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Helen_Meles.jpg/170px-Helen_Meles.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="263" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Helen_Meles.jpg/255px-Helen_Meles.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Helen_Meles.jpg/340px-Helen_Meles.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1372" data-file-height="2120"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Helen_Meles.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Eritrean artist <a href="/wiki/Helen_Meles" title="Helen Meles">Helen Meles</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Eritrea" title="Music of Eritrea">Music of Eritrea</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Eritrea's ethnic groups each have their own styles of music and accompanying dances. Amongst the Tigrinya, the best known traditional musical genre is the guaila. Traditional instruments of Eritrean folk music include the stringed <a href="/wiki/Krar" title="Krar">krar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kebero" title="Kebero">kebero</a>, <a href="/wiki/Begena" title="Begena">begena</a>, <a href="/wiki/Masenqo" title="Masenqo">masenqo</a> and the wata (a distant/rudimentary cousin of the violin). A popular Eritrean artist is the Tigrinya singer <a href="/wiki/Helen_Meles" title="Helen Meles">Helen Meles</a>, who is noted for her powerful voice and wide singing range.<sup id="cite_ref-Blum_203-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Blum-203">[203]</a></sup> Other prominent local musicians include the Kunama singer <a href="/wiki/Dehab_Faytinga" title="Dehab Faytinga">Dehab Faytinga</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ruth_Abraha" title="Ruth Abraha">Ruth Abraha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bereket_Mengisteab" title="Bereket Mengisteab">Bereket Mengisteab</a>, the late <a href="/wiki/Yemane_Ghebremichael" title="Yemane Ghebremichael">Yemane Ghebremichael</a>, and the late <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Afewerki" title="Abraham Afewerki">Abraham Afewerki</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Eritrea" title="Sport in Eritrea">Sport in Eritrea</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Tour_of_Asmara_Cycling_race,_Asmara_Eritrea.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Tour_of_Asmara_Cycling_race%2C_Asmara_Eritrea.jpg/240px-Tour_of_Asmara_Cycling_race%2C_Asmara_Eritrea.jpg" decoding="async" width="240" height="160" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Tour_of_Asmara_Cycling_race%2C_Asmara_Eritrea.jpg/360px-Tour_of_Asmara_Cycling_race%2C_Asmara_Eritrea.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Tour_of_Asmara_Cycling_race%2C_Asmara_Eritrea.jpg/480px-Tour_of_Asmara_Cycling_race%2C_Asmara_Eritrea.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5472" data-file-height="3648"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Tour_of_Asmara_Cycling_race,_Asmara_Eritrea.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Tour_of_Eritrea" title="Tour of Eritrea">Tour of Eritrea</a> cycling competition in <a href="/wiki/Asmara" title="Asmara">Asmara</a>, Eritrea.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Football</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tour_of_Eritrea" title="Tour of Eritrea">cycling</a> are the most popular sports in Eritrea. Cycling has a long tradition in Eritrea and was first introduced during the colonial period.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">[205]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Tour_of_Eritrea" title="Tour of Eritrea">Tour of Eritrea</a>, a multi-stage cycling event, is held annually since 1946 throughout the country. </p>
      <p>The national cycling teams of both men and women are ranked first on the <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">African</a> continent, and Eritrea is ranked among the best cycling nations in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">[206]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Eritrea national cycling team has experienced a lot of success, winning the African continental cycling championship several years in a row. In 2013, the women's team won the gold medal in the <a href="/wiki/African_Continental_Cycling_Championships" class="mw-redirect" title="African Continental Cycling Championships">African Continental Cycling Championships</a> for the first time, and for the second time in 2015 and third time in 2019. The men's team have won gold 7 times in the last 9 years in the African continental cycling championships, between 2010 and 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">[208]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">[209]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">[210]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>More than six Eritrean riders have signed professional contracts to international cycling teams, including <a href="/wiki/Natnael_Berhane" title="Natnael Berhane">Natnael Berhane</a> and <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Teklehaimanot" title="Daniel Teklehaimanot">Daniel Teklehaimanot</a>. Berhane was named African Sportsman of the Year in 2013, while Teklehaimanot became the first Eritrean to ride the <a href="/wiki/Vuelta_a_Espa%C3%B1a" title="Vuelta a EspaÃ±a">Vuelta a EspaÃ±a</a> in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-Cnbcfertf_211-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cnbcfertf-211">[211]</a></sup> In 2015, Teklehaimanot won the King of the Mountains classification in the <a href="/wiki/2015_Crit%C3%A9rium_du_Dauphin%C3%A9" title="2015 CritÃ©rium du DauphinÃ©">CritÃ©rium du DauphinÃ©</a>. Teklehaimanot and fellow Eritrean <a href="/wiki/Merhawi_Kudus" title="Merhawi Kudus">Merhawi Kudus</a> became the first black cyclists from <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a> to compete in the <a href="/wiki/Tour_de_France" title="Tour de France">Tour de France</a>, when they were selected by the <a href="/wiki/Team_Qhubeka_Assos" title="Team Qhubeka Assos">MTNâQhubeka</a> team for the <a href="/wiki/2015_Tour_de_France" title="2015 Tour de France">2015 edition</a> of the race.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">[212]</a></sup> In July of the year, Teklehaimanot also became the first rider from an African team to wear the <a href="/wiki/Mountains_classification_in_the_Tour_de_France" title="Mountains classification in the Tour de France">polka dot jersey</a> at the Tour de France.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">[213]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Eritrean athletes have also seen increasing success in the international arena in other sports. <a href="/wiki/Zersenay_Tadese" title="Zersenay Tadese">Zersenay Tadese</a>, an Eritrean athlete, formerly held the world record in the half marathon.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">[214]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ghirmay_Ghebreslassie" title="Ghirmay Ghebreslassie">Ghirmay Ghebreslassie</a> became the first Eritrean to win a gold medal at a <a href="/wiki/World_Championships_in_Athletics" class="mw-redirect" title="World Championships in Athletics">World Championships in Athletics</a> for his country when he took the <a href="/wiki/2015_World_Championships_in_Athletics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_marathon" title="2015 World Championships in Athletics â Men's marathon">marathon</a> at the <a href="/wiki/2015_World_Championships_in_Athletics" title="2015 World Championships in Athletics">2015 World Championships</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">[215]</a></sup> Eritrea made its Winter Olympic debut 25 February 2018, when they competed at the <a href="/wiki/2018_Winter_Olympics" title="2018 Winter Olympics">2018 Winter Olympics</a> in <a href="/wiki/Pyeongchang" class="mw-redirect" title="Pyeongchang">Pyeongchang</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a> 2018. Eritrea's team was represented by their flagbearer <a href="/wiki/Shannon-Ogbnai_Abeda" title="Shannon-Ogbnai Abeda">Shannon-Ogbnai Abeda</a> who competed as <a href="/wiki/Alpine_skier" class="mw-redirect" title="Alpine skier">alpine skier</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">[216]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eritrea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
